vague and indistinct.
Indistinct and vague,
yet within it there are forms;
vague and indistinct,
yet within it there are things.
Deep and dark,
yet within it there is essence.
Its essence is most true,
and within it there is authenticity.
From ancient times to now,
its name does not fade,
as it oversees all things.

How do I know the state of all things?
By this.

The Container of the Great Virtue
is the Dark Gateway’s aperture.
The ancients said:
*"One aperture, the Dark Gateway’s hole—
Heaven and Earth together formed it.
Within it hides the divine qi’s cavern,
named the yin-yang essence."*

Again it is said:
*"One aperture, the Dark Gateway’s great door—
Here, lead is forged and cinnabar refined."*

*The Classic of Changes* says:
*"These two apertures’ methods—
the metallic qi also harmonizes with them."*

Thus the Dao speaks of *"the Gate of the Dark Mother,"*
the Confucian of *"the Gate of Principle and Righteousness,"*
the Buddha of *"the Gate of Non-Duality."*

All are but the Container of the Great Virtue’s capacity:
Heaven, Earth, and all things
are born from within it.
It is neither empty nor non-empty,
neither the Dao nor non-Dao—
empty and the Dao are one.
Empty and the Dao do not separate.
Without emptiness, there is no Dao;
without the Dao, there is no emptiness.
Thus it is said:
*"It follows only the Dao."*

If one seeks the Dao,
and abandons this empty vessel—
where else shall they seek?

But emptiness without form
is mere vulgar emptiness.
How then shall the student gather medicine and refine the elixir?

It must be empty yet containing ultimate reality,
nonexistent yet encompassing ultimate existence—
only then does it avoid one-sided learning.

The practitioner, having set aside all concerns,
rests quietly for a moment,
observing this aperture.
Indistinct, as if nonexistent;
vague, as if something.
In the depths of emptiness and stillness,
the divine spark moves—
the formless becomes formed.
This is the radiance of the Self’s nature,
the floating of wood and fire—
the initial stirrings of the subtle yang.

Again, with this divine light’s fleeting movement,
contain it with the gaze and direct it downward.
Vague, as if aware;
indistinct, as if knowing nothing—
within it, the yang essence stirs—
this is when the light of yin first meets the palace of yin.

At this time, the vital force is weak,
beyond taking.
Only the two stages of the *Adopted Mother* method
adjust and regulate the errant yin-qi,
meeting in the aperture’s center.
One stage for adjustment and extraction,
one for returning to the furnace and nourishing.

Following the method without pause,
fire enters water’s depths,
water’s gold is born—
dim and dark, unknown in its extremity,
this is when the divine qi merges
and the yin-yang essence is generated.

Yet when true essence is born,
the body stands like a wall,
the mind like cold ashes—
naturally, the whole body softens and rejoices,
the essence of limbs and body
all return to the Dark Aperture.

There is great authenticity here—
melted like ice thawing,
vast like a tide rising.
Not like before, indistinct and vague,
unnameable.

This true essence
is truly the One Essence,
not the later-Heaven mingled essence that can be compared.
It is also the original essence
from which Heaven, Earth, and all things first emerged—
the common true essence of all.

Like the winter solstice’s yang,
the child’s hour at midnight,
the success of a year and a day—
though not limited to this,
the vital force’s movements all begin here.

As if a thousand-layered tower
begins with a clod of earth,
a ten-thousand-li journey
begins with a single step.

This is the root of Heaven, Earth, and all things’ generation.
If the source is misplaced,
what extremity will the outcome reach?

Thus, from ancient times to now,
all who cultivate the Dao
never depart from gathering this true qi—
only then do the signs of life emerge.

Examining all things at their birth,
none differ from this single true essence,
forming shapes and bodies.

And how do I know all things share this?
Because within this empty aperture,
true qi accumulates.
Over time, the Dark Gateway opens
and true essence is born.

In essence,
vagueness is the density of light,
indistinctness is the subtlety of the mechanism.
Within the indistinct and vague—
the true yin of the yin-center
is the thing.

「The true yang within the **Kan** center—
this is the essence of the **Yao-Ming**,
the subtle and profound.

The scholar must know this true essence,
and only then can the practice reach its utmost.

This vague and indistinct is the nature of light’s effulgent transcendence,
thus it is said, *“there is form”* (**有象**);
this indistinct and vague is the nature of light’s downward illumination upon the **Kan** palace,
where true yang stirs to motion,
thus it is said, *“there is substance”* (**有物**).

The essence of **Yao-Ming**—
this is the essence of the **Five Agents** (**二五**), hence it is called *most true* (**甚真**).

To obtain this true essence,
one must first know true faith (**真信**).

True faith is when yin and yang alternate in their movements,
never missing the timing of their shifts.
When the moment of true faith first arrives,
the response must be precise and unerring,
then the work of **seizing and subduing** (**擒伏**) will be achieved.

When ordinary people first begin cultivation,
they must necessarily pass through vague and indistinct **Yao-Ming**,
before the impure desires cease,
and the natural principle (**天理**) remains constant.
The common breath (**凡息**) halts,
and the true breath (**真息**) appears.

Why is this so?
Because the human heart is too bright,
and awareness arises too easily.

If one reaches **Yao-Ming**,
where awareness does not stir,
then the original nature (**元性**) and original life (**元命**)
merge into one.

This very vague and indistinct **Yao-Ming**—
it is the essential key for cultivators.
When the student sits in stillness and clarity (**静定**),
suddenly, a fleeting awareness arises,
at this time, the spirit-qi (**神气**) condenses in the **elixir field** (**丹田**),
pure and unified,
and the student also does not know where it leads.
This is the nature and life returning to the **limitless void** (**无极**) of Heaven.

Though there is this external principle (**外有是理**),
within the **elixir field** (**丹田**), there must also be a harmonized **qi mechanism** (**融和气机**),
only then is it true evidence.

From this single point of harmonization,
gathered back into the **refining furnace** (**归炉**),
sealed and nurtured with warmth,
it will naturally emerge as the **true yang**—a single breath of **qi**.

But when the practice reaches this stage,
there is great peril.
Only by guarding with a single mind (**一心内守**),
and illuminating the center (**了照当中**),
can it be unified as the **elixir medicine** (**丹药**),
thus attaining longevity and immortality (**长生不老**).

If one harbors another thought (**生一它念**),
this very **original qi** (**元气**)
will already be mixed with the **post-heaven** (**后天**)
and will no longer be pure.

If one indulges in a single lustful thought (**动一淫思**),
this **qi mechanism** will scatter outward,
and the true essence (**真精**) will leak away.

The ancients said:
*The matter of leaking essence (**泄精**)—
it is not necessary to be with husband and wife,
even a single thought’s movement,
and the true essence will no longer be contained within the body,
as if fleeing like running **dan**.*

The student must make the heart and **qi** unified (**心与气合**),
and the breath and spirit intertwined (**息与神交**),
constantly dwelling in this **cavity** (**腔子**).
With time,
endless delight (**无穷趣味**) will naturally arise.

Yet this is truly difficult;
If one can penetrate the **mysterious mechanism** (**玄机**),
then there will be no difficulty.

「Initially, one merely employs the method of **lifting and nudging** (**提掇**), forbidding this point of true **qi** (**真气**) from dispersing downward, nor allowing this true **qi** to scatter among the six sense gates (**六根门头**). It is all about a single-hearted return to **fate** (**皈命**), and the five bodies (**五体**) offering sincere allegiance.

With time, one’s **true essence** (**真精**) will naturally be full and free from lustful thoughts (**不思色**).
May the student preserve and guard the **original essence** (**元精**), not allowing it to leak even a drop.

At first, it is difficult to always practice the **familiar Dao** (**熟道**).
But if one can endure again and again (**一忍再忍**), and not allow even a single thought to stir (**不许念头稍动**), within three months, the **external yang** (**外阳**) will naturally withdraw and be contained.

When the **external yang** is withdrawn and contained,
then one will see that the **original essence** (**元气**) within the body is abundant,
and the **immortal** (**长生不老**) and **transcendent** (**人仙**) will thus be attained—
for what is transcendence so distant after all?

**Chapter Twenty-Two: Fully Returning to Itself**
*"When bent, it is whole; when twisted, it becomes straight. When hollowed, it overflows; when worn, it renews. When few, it suffices; when many, it confuses."*
Thus, the **sage** (**圣人**) embraces **Oneness** (**抱一**) as a model for the world.

By not seeing oneself, one becomes bright (**不自见故明**);
By not asserting oneself, one becomes evident (**不自是故彰**);
By not praising oneself, one attains merit (**不自伐故有功**);
By not boasting of oneself, one endures (**不自矜故长**).

For only by not contending does one ensure that none in the world can contend with them.
What the ancients called *"When bent, it is whole"*—
is this not true?

Indeed, it is **whole** and **returns** to itself.
The essence of the **Great Dao** (**大道**) lies in reaching the **void** (**无**) while containing the **ultimate** (**至有**);
Returning the **ultimate** to the **void** (**至无**), only then does one attain the **method of dual cultivation** (**性命双修**).

For **nature** (**性**) is fundamentally **void** (**无**), yet **void** arises from **ultimate** (**有**);
**fate** (**命**) is fundamentally **ultimate** (**有**), yet **ultimate** arises from **void** (**无**).
If one clings to **void** (**虚无**), one falls into dull emptiness (**顽空**);
If one clings to **ultimate** (**实有**), one becomes ensnared by **forms and names** (**拘名象**).
Even if one does not descend into false and unorthodox delusions (**妄诞不经**),
it is still a one-sided practice (**一边之学**), ultimately unable to equal the **Great Dao** (**大道**).

The practitioner must first lay down all **ten thousand entanglements** (**万缘**), and not stain themselves with even a speck of **dust** (**纤尘**).
Within **Oneness** (**一**) and **having nothing** (**无所有**),
one must seek out a single spark of **life-force** (**生机**) to serve as the **elixir foundation** (**丹本**).
This is what the ancients called **true yang** (**真阳**), also known as **true lead** (**真铅**), or **true One-essence** (**真一之气**).

The **Supreme Sage** (**太上**) said: *"When bent, it is whole"*—
meaning that within the body’s hidden depths (**隐微**), the realm of **solitary knowing and solitary awareness** (**独知独觉**),
there exists a **complete, pristine, and fluid** (**浑沦完全、活泼流通**) **mechanism** (**机**).
By preserving and nurturing this,
refining and distilling it,
one can reach **elixir completion** (**丹成**) and **transcendence** (**仙就**).

The ancients likened it to the **slightest thread of yang** (**冬至一线微阳**) at the Winter Solstice,
which brings forth **unceasing life** (**生生不已**).
Or they likened it to the **first three days’ crescent moon** (**初三一弯新月**),
gradually waxing full until the fifteenth day (**十五月圆**),
all signifying the meaning of **wholeness through bending** (**由曲而全**).

For **bending** is **hidden** (**曲隐**), and in the hidden depths (**隐微**),
the **mechanism** (**机**) is subtle,
yet its **fulfillment** (**成**) is grand.
As the *Zhongyong* says: *"When bent, it can have"* (**曲能有**), and this is indeed so.

Within the **bending** (**一曲**), all is the **essence of principle and qi** (**理气之元**);
In the **whole** (**全体**), all is the **refined essence of the Great Ultimate** (**太极之粹**).
Thus, *"When bent, it is whole"* (**曲则全**).

The **sage** (**圣人**) having discovered this **bending** (**曲**), diligently and cautiously guards it,
circling and containing it like a hen brooding her egg (**如鸡温卵**),
or a dragon nurturing its pearl (**如龙养珠**).
With a single-hearted inward vigilance (**一心内守**), they do not allow it to be exposed externally (**不许外露**).

In time, it becomes vast as the tides (**浩浩如潮**),
rising and ascending upward (**逆而上伸**).
A single surge of **clear and rigid qi** (**清刚之气**) stands firm and ascends straight,
transcending the **sphere of sun and moon** (**日月之表**),
encompassing the **boundaries of heaven and earth** (**天地之外**).

The *Kun* hexagram says:
*"When the earth reaches its utmost softness, it moves and becomes hard"* (**坤至柔而动也刚**),
all from the **residue of bending** (**致曲之余**),
hidden and dormant in the **cauldron of earth** (**土釜**).
It accumulates until it overflows the heavens (**滔天**),
bursting forth unstoppably (**勃不可遏**).
Such is its nature.

Moreover, **twistedness** (**枉**) becomes **yin** (**阴**) and **softness** (**柔**), yet this is the same **qi** (**气**);
**straightness** (**直**) becomes **yang** (**阳**) and **rigidity** (**刚**), yet this is also the same **qi** (**气**).
Though it is said to transform from **twisted to straight** (**由枉而直**),
in truth, it is **both twisted and straight** (**即枉即直**).

After penetrating the **hidden depths** (**隐曲**) and uncovering the **root source** (**本源**),
its **manifestation** (**见**) becomes easy,
but **guarding** it is difficult (**为守则难**).
Only by **refining it gently** (**优焉游焉**),
nurturing its **initial traces** (**端倪**),
and further **lowering oneself** (**卑以下人**),
maintaining **humility** (**谦**) in self-cultivation (**自待**),
can one avoid the **restless and violent** (**躁暴急迫**) nature,
prevent **erroneous perceptions** (**邪见**), and
not stir **mundane fire** (**凡火**).
Only then can one forge the **golden elixir** (**金丹**).

Thus, one **controls the qi with the spirit** (**以神驭气**), and **unites the spirit with the qi** (**以气合神**),
hidden yet manifest without trace (**隐显无端**), changing yet unmeasurable (**变化莫测**).
This is the *"ultimate sincerity without pause"* (**至诚无息**),
*"embodying things without omission"* (**体物无遗**),
*"present in all yet not in any"* (**无在而无不在**).
How can it be anything but **overflowing** (**盈**)?

Yet one must be **humble** (**谦**) to receive benefit,
and **hollowed** (**洼**) to become **full** (**为盈**).
Otherwise, how could one contain all **ultimate** (**万有**)?

As for this **slightest spark of bending** (**一曲之微**),
it is all part of one’s **original nature** (**本来之物**).
This is what is meant by *"worn"* (**敝**),
for *"worn"* is also *"old"* (**敝即故**).
As the *Zhongyong* says: *"To review the old and know the new"* (**温故而知新**).

If the student wishes to obtain **news** (**新闻**) and generate **new intentions** (**新意**),
they must not neglect to **review the old** (**故有**) and **nurture it** (**温之**).
Only then can they attain the **new** (**新**).
This is also *"worn yet renewed"* (**敝即新**).

Though *"worn"* is little (**敝亦无几**),
if one nurtures it in its **fewness** (**少而养之**),
the **vast and harmonious qi** (**浩然之气**) can fill heaven and earth,
and pierce the **Big Dipper** (**贯斗牛**).

If one claims the **Dao** is vast and all-encompassing (**浩潮弥纶**),
that it is **present in all yet not in any** (**无在不是**),
and takes its **many** (**多**) aspects to practice,
I fear **principle and desire** (**理欲**) will become **entangled** (**杂乘**),
and **good and evil** (**善恶**) will be **indistinguishable** (**莫辨**).
Sometimes guarding the **middle** (**守中**), sometimes collecting **medicinal herbs** (**采药**),
sometimes advancing **fire** (**进火**) and retreating **symbols** (**退符**),
clinging to **forms** (**着象**) and grasping **names** (**执名**),
the more one does, the better (**多多益善**),
yet it remains a **rootless practice** (**无本之学**),
having not attained **cessation and return** (**止归**),
and is ultimately a **tangle of confusion** (**一个迷团**).
No wonder one remains **lifelong in doubt, never enlightened** (**毕生怀疑莫悟**).

The **sage** (**圣人**) embraces **Oneness** (**抱一**) for self-cultivation (**自修**),
and also applies it to the world (**施之天下**),
as a **model for all** (**天下楷模**).
If one does not know that the **method of bending** (**一曲之道**) is truly the **unifying method** (**一贯之道**),
and occasionally strays from it—
**occasional straying** (**偶离**) means **no model** (**无式**),
**no model** means **no attainment** (**无成**),
and the **Dao** is thus **unreliable** (**何赖焉**).

For the **Dao** is fundamentally **one principle of heaven and humanity** (**天人一理**),
**all things share the same source** (**物我同源**),
and is **common to all** (**公共之物**).
Yet today’s students each **cling stubbornly to their own views** (**固执己见**),
claiming none can surpass them (**谓人莫己若**).
Even this **boastful thought** (**矜骄之念**) has already obscured their **innate clarity** (**灵明**),
and they do not understand to **measure the ancient and apply it to the present** (**酌古准今**),
nor to **take the law from its highest source** (**取法乎上**).

The *Zhongyong* says:
*"The **Dao of the gentleman** is **darkly luminous** (**暗然**) and naturally stands forth"* (**自章**),
*"The **Dao of the petty person** is **brightly evident** (**的然**) and naturally perishes"* (**自亡**).

「The **Dao** of the true cultivator is indeed something to be held with solemn reverence. Even if one approaches the brink of divine transformation, it is merely what one ought to achieve by duty and nature—why must one display it to the world and boast of one’s accomplishments? If one praises oneself, not only will others despise it, but the merit itself will be false and not genuine. The ancients, after achieving their goals, withdrew humbly, never claiming credit for their deeds; it is fitting that their merit should cover the world and serve as a model for all ages.

As for self-cultivation and self-discipline, it is like clothing that brings warmth or food that satisfies hunger—each person attains their own comfort and joy, and what others possess is sufficient for them. Why should one be arrogant and self-conceited, boasting of one’s strengths? Though it is said that wisdom grows daily and insight expands each day, this is merely a common trait of human nature—only that I have attained it earlier. Where is the true merit in that?

If one boasts of their strengths, then those strengths will become weaknesses. Even the most foolish person would not willingly fall behind—how many disputes do not originate from this? The gentleman has no need to contend, so the world cannot contend with his ability. The ancient saying, *"Bend and you will remain whole"* (**曲则全**), is indeed not empty words—does it not mean that one must fully receive and fully return to attain the **Dao**? This is the **Zhongyong**’s **Dao**, and the next level is the **Dao** of bending (**致曲**), which is hidden yet profound (**隐曲**).

The **Dao** is called *"**Xuanqiao**"* (**玄窍**), the Buddha calls it *"**Nagaraja**"* (**那个**), and the Confucian calls it *"**duanni**"* (**端倪**). Though it is not void nor empty, it is the origin from which heaven and earth opened, and all beings emerged. At every moment, its movement and stillness are visible.

When it is still and gives rise, it does not come from external stimulation—
suddenly one becomes aware, and this awareness itself is bending (**曲**).
When it moves and manifests, it arises from spontaneous resonance—
suddenly it stirs, and this stirring itself is bending (**曲**).
Essentially, all comes from a time of ignorance and unawareness,
when the **qi**’s momentum moves on its own.
It moves and suddenly one is aware—this is true movement, true awareness.
But its momentum is extremely subtle, fleeting in an instant;
a mere shift of thought or breath is already **postnatal** (**后天**),
and cannot serve as the root of life for beings,
nor as the foundation for refining the elixir (**炼丹**).

We receive **qi** and take form as beings and things—
all from this single moment of differentiation.
The right and wrong, true and false of **Dao** cultivation—
which does not originate from this single moment?
*The Zhou Shu* says:
*"**Wàngniàn** (**罔念**) leads to madness, **kèniàn** (**克念**) leads to sainthood."*
The difference between sainthood and madness is decided by this single moment—
so swift, this is what is meant by bending (**一曲**).

The ancients likened it to lightning and the flash of a stone,
or to riding a thousand-li horse that leaves the dust behind and gallops on.
At this moment, one must have the **Buddha’s wisdom eye** (**智珠**) brightly illuminating
to recognize it clearly.
Once this **origin** (**端倪**) is known,
one must still nourish and expand it—
as Mencius said: *"Fire begins with a spark, water with a trickle,
yet they grow vast and fill the heavens and earth."*

But how does one expand?
It is not by forcing oneself to submit—
only then can **true qi** (**正气**) stretch naturally.
It is not by lowering oneself artificially—
only then can **heavenly virtue** (**天德**) remain whole.
One must only guard the **Dao**’s original state within things,
unmixed and undivided,
warm in its stillness,
embracing **oneness** (**一**),
not seeking novelty in new ends,
nor indulging in the complexity of names and forms (**名象**).
Thus, one will not fall deeper into confusion with each passing day,
but instead find joy in the **Dao**’s ceaseless renewal (**日新又新**).

The ancient sages knew that bending (**一曲**) is the stage for attaining immortality and sainthood,
so they embraced **qi** with the **Dao**,
let the **Dao** depend on **qi**,
and united **Dao** and **qi** without separation,
as the essential method for self-cultivation,
and as the model for all under heaven.
If one insists on their own views,
then they obscure their own clarity and fail to shine.
What’s more, self-praise leads to labor without merit,
and self-conceit leads to shortcoming rather than growth.

Wisdom arises from emotion (**智起情生**),
often becoming the **Dao**’s greatest harm.
Only by not insisting on one’s own views,
not praising oneself nor boasting of one’s strengths,
can one’s mind remain tranquil and **qi** harmonious—
then naturally, there will be no evil outside,
no exhaustion within,
and who will contend with them?

The **Dao**’s subtle and silent transformation is thus:
unless one embraces **oneness** (**抱一**) and fully receives and returns,
how can one return to the **Taishang**’s (**太始**) original beginning?

**Chapter 23: Rare Speech and Naturalness**
Rare speech and naturalness (**希言自然**).
Hence, gusts of wind do not last all morning,
sudden rains do not persist all day.
Who is responsible for this?
Heaven and earth.
Even heaven and earth cannot endure long—
how much less so humanity?
Thus, those who practice the **Dao**:
those aligned with the **Dao** are in harmony with the **Dao**,
those aligned with **virtue** (**德**) are in harmony with **virtue**,
those aligned with loss are in harmony with loss.
Those in harmony with the **Dao** find the **Dao** rejoices in their attainment;
those in harmony with **virtue** find **virtue** rejoices in their attainment;
those in harmony with loss find loss rejoices in their attainment—
truly, there is no doubt,
there is no disbelief.

The **Dao** is fundamentally without sound or breath (**无声无息**),
so it is called *"**rare speech**"* (**希言**).
The **Dao** is fundamentally without action or contrivance (**无为无作**),
so it is called *"**naturalness**"* (**自然**).

What can endure, what can last—
it is nothing but following heaven’s movement and acting in accordance with one’s nature,
listening solely to the **qi**’s momentum as it unfolds.
If one forces or fabricates, unable to follow the **qi**’s momentum,
and fails to align with the **Heaven-Earth**’s (**乾坤**) revolving cycles,
the rising and setting of the sun and moon,
then it will be like fleeting winds of boiling soup,
violent torrents of rain—
uprooting great trees, surging across flat plains,
coming swiftly, departing swiftly—
how could their force endure all day or all morning?

Yet who is responsible for this?
Ask heaven and earth, and they will not know.
For heaven and earth are the sovereign rulers of all things—
if they do not follow their own constant ways,
they still cannot endure long.
How much less so humanity, which exists within heaven and earth,
like a single grain in the **Taicang** (**太仓**)?
If one does not practice the **Dao**’s enduring way,
how can they hope to last?

Thus, the **Taishang** (**太上**) teaches that the **Dao**’s source
is **wuwei** (**无为**) as its essence,
and naturalness (**自然**) as its function.
If one does not attend to this,
but instead boasts of shortcuts,
or seeks out marvelous tricks,
one is mistaken!

Observe those who study the **Dao**—
though they may dwell in distant east, west, south, or north,
and their teachings vary in sound,
yet if they have a resolve for the **Dao**,
and do not stray into false paths,
they will all converge in perfect accord without division.»

To walk the Dao and gain insight within—this is called **virtue**.
Once one knows how to cultivate the Dao,
**virtue** naturally arises within them.
All who clearly manifest their **virtue**,
free from distraction and confusion,
find themselves in silent accord as one.

Thus it is said:
*"Those who align with the Dao are one with the Dao,
those who align with **virtue** are one with **virtue**—
what strange wonder is there in this?"*

At the outset of practice,
cultivation follows the Dao and **virtue**,
adheres to principles and rules,
effortless yet unburdened, free from entanglement.
When one reaches the stage of profound self-realization,
settled in ease and deepened in insight,
resources flow effortlessly in all directions—
what was once gained now seems suddenly lost.
With pure dedication, all merges into one,
as though crafting a wheel behind closed doors,
yet when it rolls, the rims align perfectly—
all is unified.
Thus it is said:
*"Those who lose are one with loss."*

These three stages differ in their effort,
each advancing along distinct paths.
Yet when the labor endures long,
and suffering fades into tranquility,
a boundless serenity emerges,
rich with delight—
spontaneously expressing the natural workings of heaven.
Suffering is exhausted—
where then does joy find its limit?
Thus it is said:
*"Those who align with the Dao find the Dao rejoices in them;
those who align with **virtue** find **virtue** rejoices in them;
those who align with loss find loss rejoices in them."*

Clearly, the essence of **wuwei** is what all cultivate together,
and the art of naturalness is what all employ in common.
Even sages spanning ten thousand *li*,
or divine beings across ten thousand years—
though time and place may shift,
they naturally harmonize as though seals fit perfectly,
all converging toward the same path.

If one claims that naturalness is not always thus,
then delusion obstructs within,
and strange methods arise.
Some cling rigidly to the concrete, stubbornly fixed,
others cling to emptiness, practicing solitary stillness.
Such cases are countless—
all stem from failing to trust the principle of **wuwei**,
the Dao of naturalness,
and instead clinging to their own views as truth.

No wonder those who begin young in the Dao
find no fruition in their later years—
their resolve exceeds their learning,
yet they never grasp the true meaning,
straying into false paths.
How tragic!
How lamentable!

This speaks of the **Dao of wuwei** and naturalness—
the same that governs heaven and earth, sun and moon,
the unseen and the spirits of the dead and living.
All follow this principle:
**wuwei** and naturalness,
where birth is fulfillment,
and action is spontaneous use.

Yet ordinary people, once born,
exhaust their cleverness day and night—
how much of their innate **Dao** remains?
Only those of lofty **Dao** follow nature’s constant way.

Though their early efforts may seem forced,
once perfected, they return to the realm of **wuwei** and naturalness,
as if effortless—
without striving, yet hitting the mark,
moving freely along the **Dao**.

Thus, the sage observing the Great **Dao** sees
the principle of **wuwei** and naturalness
clearly before their eyes—
no need for agreement, yet all align.
But common folk, gazing at the Great **Dao**,
believe only sages and immortals dare speak of it;
ordinary people dare not.

The *Zhongyong* says:
*"Strive in learning, struggle in difficulty—
success brings unity."*
Is this mere deceit?
No.

---

Yet the root of this lies in the initial unbelief in the **Dao** of *wuwei* and naturalness,
entering through the gate of *budaode* (not the Way).
The further one strays, the deeper the separation—
thus, the **Dao** of *wuwei* and naturalness cannot be fully embraced,
and distinctions arise like divided households.

Only those who grasp this principle
will not be misled by false paths and heterodox teachings.

**Chapter Twenty-Four: The Perils of Self-Imposed Extremes**
He who stands on tiptoe cannot stand firm,
he who strides cannot walk steadily.
He who insists on his own view sees nothing clearly,
he who clings to his own righteousness cannot shine forth.
He who boasts of his own merits gains no true success,
he who vaunts his own virtues cannot endure.

In the **Dao**, such actions are called
superfluous food and burdensome exertion.
Men may detest them, hence the **Dao**-bearer does not indulge.

Earlier, it was said that the **Dao** is spoken of rarely and naturally,
not like the world’s coarse and dull masses,
who mistake idleness for *wuwei* and reckless abandon for naturalness.

Truly, this is the **Dao** of Great Balance and Rectitude,
conforming to Heaven’s principle and human nature,
following the sage’s path and the kingly **Way**,
preserving and reflecting upon the origin,
returning to the source—
thus, in harmony with Heaven’s command,
there is *wuwei* yet nothing remains undone,
naturalness yet nothing unnatural.

The *Yijing* says: *"To exhaust principle and fulfill nature, reaching even to fate"*—
this must be the man of **Dao**!

Excess is fault, deficiency is also fault.
The *Shujing* states: *"Without partiality or cliques, the kingly **Way** flows vast and unrestricted"*—
this is indeed the case.

Even as a man stands upright,
there is an original constancy that does not alter.
The *tiptoeing* (跂) is when both feet are raised in support.
The *Shijing* says: *"On tiptoe, I await him"*—
with this stance, one may gaze far and wide,
but if it is meant to endure, how can it last?

The *striding* (跨) is when both feet are spread apart.
With this, one may ride astride a horse and rest upon the saddle,
but if it is meant for walking, how can it proceed?
The enlightened do not cling to their own views—
clinging to one’s own view, clarity is lost.
The illustrious do not insist on their own sight—
insisting on one’s own sight, brilliance is obscured.

Often, those who boast of their own merits reap no true success,
for success that is genuine cannot be concealed by others—
why boast at all?
Often, those who vaunt their own virtues cannot last,
for virtues that endure command natural reverence—
why need to vaunt?

If one does not believe in the **Dao** of *wuwei* and naturalness,
and does not know how *"without doing, yet all things are done"* (莫之为而为),
*"without striving, yet all things are achieved"* (莫之致而致),
then all actions are left to Heaven—
how effortless!

To move yet cannot help but move,
to stop yet cannot help but stop—
movement and stillness blend in effortless spontaneity,
how tranquil!

If one fails to grasp the void yet without trace (虚而无朕),
it is like being vast yet unable to contain—
or if one adds an extra thought,
or forces an additional perspective,
like gluttony’s excess or labor’s overstrain—
not only is it unprofitable, but it harms.

The scholar must align with the *wuwei* of Heaven’s **virtue**,
follow the *ziran* (自然) of things’ inherent principle—
not only should one not impose human contrivances upon it,
but even things themselves should be allowed their ease.

Regulate one’s diet and rest—
if even slightly mismatched, exceeding the natural measure,
whether through overindulgence or excessive asceticism—
like a dog’s overstuffed belly bringing injury,
or a cow’s overworked body bringing exhaustion—
this is to invite inner unrest and self-detestation.

Hence it is said: *"Men may detest them."*

Those who twist and strain, seeking to stand or walk,
to shine or be illustrious,
to achieve merits that move others,
or virtues that surpass the crowd—
such endeavors are indeed difficult!

The **Dao**-bearing gentleman despises them utterly,
deeming them unworthy of his own company.

This rare mention of naturalness
is but one principle: **cleanness** (清净).

What is **cleanness** (清)?
When not a single thought arises.

What is **purity** (净)?
When not a speck of dust defiles the mind.

The goal is for this heart
to be like a mirror without dust,
or still water without ripples—
a single luminous, empty spirit,
and **cleanness** is attained.

If the world’s common folk,
dull and muddled, spend the day doing nothing,
this is not **cleanness**.

Only when **cleanness** holds light,
and **purity** reflects brilliance,
like a moonlit pool’s unobstructed radiance—
then does one truly grasp **cleanness**.

Yet if even a trace of self-display or self-righteousness remains,
it becomes an obstruction.

Thus, the seeker of the **Dao** must cultivate a boundless heart,
letting no thing or thought disturb his mind or occupy his spirit.
Through prolonged nurturing, a single luminous spark
illuminates all—
like the sun and moon in the sky,
penetrating every corner.

Only fear arises when
one thought of clarity is followed by another of indulgence—
then clarity is no longer constant.

Mencius’ strength lay in *yangqi* (养气),
for when *qi* is undisturbed, the spirit is naturally luminous,
and when the spirit is luminous, the heart is naturally at ease—
thus he spoke not of nurturing the heart but of nurturing the *qi*,
truly knowing that when the will is unified, it moves the *qi*,
and when the *qi* is unified, it moves the will.

If one merely claims to nurture the heart
without seeking to nurture the *qi*,
many will never find peace in their hearts their whole lives.

When the heart is truly **cleanness** (清净),
the true *yang* (真阳) naturally arises.
All ascensions and descents, movements and transformations,
must follow their natural course.

To force the *tiptoeing* (跂) to stand,
or the *striding* (跨) to walk—
excessive food or burdensome exertion—
these are all misalignments.
Things already detest them—
how much more so will men?

Hence, the **Dao**-bearing gentleman
cannot bear to indulge in such things.

**Chapter Twenty-Fifth: The **Dao** Follows Naturalness**
There exists a primordial unity (有物混成),
born before Heaven and Earth,
silent and vast (寂兮寥兮),
self-sufficient yet unchanging (独立而不改),
circulating without exhaustion (周行而不殆),
capable of being the Mother of all under Heaven.

I do not know its name—
I call it **Dao** (道),
and forcefully name it *Great* (大).
*Great* means *passing* (逝),
*passing* means *distant* (远),
*distant* means *returning* (反).

Thus, the **Dao** is *Great*,
Heaven is *Great*,
Earth is *Great*,
and the king is also *Great*.
Within the realm, there are four *Great* ones,
and the king stands among them.

The king follows Earth,
Earth follows Heaven,
Heaven follows the **Dao**,
and the **Dao** follows naturalness (*ziran*).

What is the **Dao**?
It is the undifferentiated state before *Hongmeng* (鸿蒙) split,
when Heaven and Earth had not yet taken form,
when man and things were yet unshaped—
a boundless, chaotic *qi* (混混沌沌),

Boundless and boundless, measureless and endless,
as if there were a thing formed from the chaos,
swirling in reality, born before Heaven and Earth—
this is what is called the **Wuji** (無極).

Silent and void yet teeming with vitality,
vast yet containing motion—
this is what is called the **Taiji** (太極).

All things have duality,
yet the **Taiji** is undivided.

From its single movement,
Heaven and Earth were opened,
Yin and Yang divided,
the Four Symbols and Five Phases contained within.
Humans and things proliferate,
the sun and moon wax and wane—
how could it not be that the more they generate,
the more the **Taiji** seems to diminish?

Yet this chaotic, primordial substance—
invisible to sight, inaudible to hearing,
yet present in all things, at all times—
solitary yet complete,
wholly unified yet ever-generating,
endlessly transforming—
from chaos to the present,
unchanging in its constant measure,
flowing as one *qi* within independence,
circulating through the Dharma-realm,
opening and closing effortlessly,
cycling endlessly.

If one speaks of ordinary things,
it seems as though it might be exhausted!
Yet it flows through the Three Realms,
fills all beings,
Heaven relies on it for clarity,
Earth on stability,
valleys on fullness,
humans on life—
all following its natural course.

Within it, things generate themselves,
complete themselves,
while the **Taiji** remains wholly intact,
yet never diminished.

Though myriad transformations arise endlessly,
all emerge from it—
thus it can be the Mother of all under Heaven.

Heaven is most exalted,
and thus may be named;
Earth is most profound,
and thus may be named.
Yet this **Wuji**—the ultimate of the ultimate—
neither divine nor formless,
silent yet ceaseless—
I know not its name,
and thus call it **Dao**.

The **Dao** is the shared path of Heaven, Earth, and all beings,
the common origin.
The **Dao** encompasses Heaven and Earth,
yet Heaven and Earth cannot encompass the **Dao**.
The **Dao** nurtures all beings,
yet all beings cannot nurture the **Dao**.
Its vastness is unfathomable—
I forcefully name it *Great*.

Oh, the **Dao** is *Great*!
How it moves forward endlessly,
with nothing to halt it!
Beyond *Great* is *Passing*—
how it transcends all boundaries,
fills the absolute void,
endlessly distant and immeasurable!
Beyond *Passing* is *Distant*—
for all things, when extremes meet,
they return—
how it turns and flows,
cycling without end!
Thus it is also named *Returning*.

Such names, though varied,
can only slightly describe its grandeur.
Yet what is greater than the **Dao**?
Beyond the **Dao**, only Heaven is *Great*.
Beyond Heaven, only Earth is *Great*.
Above Earth, only the king is *Great*.
Thus, within the four directions,
there are four *Great* ones,
and the king stands among them.

The king is the first among all things,
governing rivers and mountains,
ruling over humans and things,
worthy to be named *Great* alongside Heaven and Earth.
Yet the king is borne by Earth,
so he follows Earth in governance.
Earth is covered by Heaven,
so Earth follows Heaven in decree.
And Heaven is nurtured by the **Dao**,
so Heaven follows the **Dao** in administration.
All ultimately stem from naturalness,
requiring no coercion or arrangement.
Is the **Dao** then something separate?
I forcefully name it *the **Dao** follows naturalness*.

The scholar who cultivates both nature (*xing*) and life (*ming*)
must take the *li* (principles) and *qi* of Heaven and Earth as substance,
and their functions as practice.
Thus, cultivating nature exhausts nature,
refining life establishes life—
how could mere talk of *naturalness* compare?

Heaven and Earth are vast and boundless,
encompassing both the most apparent and subtle,
the most empty and solid.
Yet all forms and colors arise from within—
what is this thing?

Born before Heaven and Earth,
governing within them,
established in purity yet unchanging,
circulating through the sands of existence without exhaustion—
truly the Mother of all under Heaven.

Before the opening of creation,
this maternal *qi* existed,
and only then did Heaven and Earth arise.
After the opening of creation,
this maternal *qi* sustained,
and only then did humans and things emerge.
I know not its name—
I forcefully call it **Dao**, call it *Great*.
*Great* encompasses all,
*Passing* reaches everywhere,
and nothing is too *Distant* to attain.

Know that extremes must return—
the **Dao**’s grandeur is not merely among the four *Great* ones!

The student of the **Dao** must not speak idly of *naturalness*,
but must instead focus the mind and regulate the breath—
focusing the mind so it does not scatter,
aligning the human heart with the heart of Heaven and Earth;
regulating the breath so it does not falter,
harmonizing human *qi* with the *qi* of Heaven and Earth.

Assisting the cosmos,
weaving through Heaven and Earth—
what greater function is there?
It lies within one’s mind and body,
a breath’s span away.

As the *Zhongyong* says:
*“Attain harmony, and Heaven and Earth take their positions,
and all things are nurtured.”*
Is this not what it means?

If one constantly nurtures the mind,
moment by moment cultivates *qi*,
and beyond mere sustenance and rest,
remains ever-aware—
allowing no stray thought, no broken breath—
only then is illness averted.
Otherwise, even a moment’s neglect invites external evils to disturb.
When right *qi* is lost,
evil *qi* easily enters—
this is inevitable.

The ancients said:
*“If one’s thoughts never arise,
desires never form,
Heaven and Earth cannot fathom their secrets,
ghosts and spirits cannot discern their workings.”*
This is no falsehood.

Some say one must first establish the foundation (*zhujī*) to attain longevity.
Yet the student of the **Dao** needs no such foundation—
only that mind and *qi* remain constantly knit as one,
never scattered,
and then ghosts and spirits cannot seize the soul or spirit.
My life is mine alone—
not by Heaven’s decree.

The Master says:
*"I do not fear the blame of divulging this—
should later scholars fail to uphold these teachings,
they will have no way to answer me.*

**Chapter Twenty-Six: The Heavy as the Light’s Root, the Still as the Restless’ Lord**
The heavy is the root of the light,
the still is the sovereign of the restless.
Thus the Sage, throughout the day,
walks without abandoning the burdened cart—
though there be splendid sights,
he rests as one detached.

Alas, how can the ruler of ten thousand chariots
hold his body so lightly to the world?
Lightness brings loss of *qi*,
restlessness brings loss of spirit.
The path of cultivation
concerns but two things: spirit and *qi*.
To refine and nourish them,
to return them to the Original Beginning’s Heaven—
this is all.

In the **pre-heaven** stage,
*qi* is undifferentiated, formless,
ever dense and settled;
spirit dwells in the shapeless,
ever subtle and ineffable.
Once entering the **post-heaven** stage,
the heavy *qi* becomes light and ascends,
the still spirit becomes restless and moves.
The *qi* is not as lively as in pre-heaven,
ever damp and murky, failing to purify;
the spirit is not as luminous as in pre-heaven,
severed from its root, yet alone it shines.
This is why life fails to take hold,
and nature becomes hard to refine.

Scholars who seek longevity
must know that *qi* must return to its root.
How can the root be restored?
The light and scattered *qi* must be
reclaimed to the realm of depth and solidity,
steadfast and unyielding,
congealed into one mass—
then *qi* returns to life,
and its vastness fills the Heaven.
The restless and deluded spirit must be
reclaimed to the land of clarity,
ever lucid and serene,
free and at ease—
then spirit returns to nature,
and its unity knows no bounds.

Thus, when spirit returns to its original nature,
and *qi* returns to its original life,
it is as though Heaven and Earth
had not yet begun to manifest—
undivided, boundless,
vast and endless.
The more it congeals and solidifies,
the swifter its movement;
the more it is empty and without trace,
the more boundless its function.

By this,
the *qi* grows ever heavy yet ever light—
this is the **Hao** and **Ran** *qi*,
most great, most resolute,
filling Heaven and Earth;
the spirit, able to be still yet also active—
as the *Yijing* says:
*"Wondrously transforming all things, it is the spirit."*
Zǐsī’s words: *"Supreme sincerity is like the spirit"*—
this is correct.

Thus the Sage, in his adherence to the **Dao**,
walks throughout the day without straying from the burdened cart,
lest his light *qi* weigh down the heavy,
and hinder the movement’s mechanism.
Such steadfast self-mastery—
does it not quicken his progress?
Even if there be the beauty of sounds and colors,
the allure of wealth and profit,
these are the splendid sights of the common folk,
not the concerns of the virtuous.

When such things appear before his eyes,
the virtuous man remains as one in seclusion,
detached from all things,
as though they do not exist.
Alas, how can he who holds the rule of ten thousand chariots,
the highest honor and rank,
a body capable of becoming an immortal or Buddha,
fail to cherish himself,
yet cling to worldly pleasures,
the joys of mortal life, as his fate?
Is this not to hold his body lightly,
and view himself as too small?

Lightness brings loss of *qi*—
*qi* lost, the form of the subject is lost;
restlessness brings loss of spirit—
spirit lost, the form of the sovereign is lost.
When both spirit and *qi* are lost,
and one claims the body can still endure—
how few there are!

This is truly to not know
that the human body is hard to obtain,
the Central Lands hard to be born in,
yet to hold oneself lightly—
is this not a great lament?

Some cling to the dusty world’s splendor,
covet the path of officialdom,
saying that those who benefit themselves are many,
and those who enrich their families are great.
Yet they do not see that
the fields of wealth and nobility
are also the lands of sword and war!
From ages past,
the elephant perished by its tusks,
the jade brought ruin by its embrace—
their harm can be counted!

How is it that men
only see the small and fail to follow the great?
Ah! This grievous indeed!"

The water is light and floats—
this is the *post-heaven qi*, an external elixir.
Gold is heavy and sinks—
this is the *pre-heaven essence*, called true lead—
also called *golden elixir*, also called the *White Tiger’s crescent qi*.
Its names vary, yet it is the internal elixir.

Pre-heaven gold generates water,
the natural order of creation,
giving life to man—
thus, *heavy is the root of light*.

Man born of *post-heaven* is but
a raging, light, and floating *qi* in action—
thus water’s *qi* is light and floats,
passions and desires multiply,
the treasure of life is lost—
hence, aging and decay come easily.

The sage has the method of *inverse cultivation*,
nothing but water giving birth to gold again,
light returning to heavy,
to restore the unity of *pre-heaven qi*.

Thus, throughout the day he walks,
never straying from his burden—
neither swaying nor tipping,
steadfast and upright,
nurturing vast *qi* to fill heaven and earth.

This is the Dao of *inverse cultivation* for the immortal,
forged through elixir refinement.
In sum, it is the transformation
from form to formlessness—
one matter of the elixir path.

Fire is dry and active—
the *post-heaven spirit*, an external elixir.
Wood is still and congealed—
the *pre-heaven essence*, called true mercury,
true essence, also called *Green Dragon*, *True One qi*.
Its names are many, yet all are internal elixirs.

Pre-heaven wood generates fire,
the natural order of creation,
giving life to man—
thus, *stillness is the sovereign of agitation*.

Once man takes form,
purely the restless, deceitful spirit of confused thought prevails—
thus fire’s nature is wild and erratic,
fraud and trickery abound,
true essence is bound and lost—
hence, weakness and collapse come easily.

The sage has the method of *inverted application*,
nothing but fire giving birth to wood again,
agitation returning to stillness,
to restore the unity of the dual spirit.

Though there may be splendor and ease,
all phenomena are empty,
one true essence is held—
nurturing the Great Awakening Golden Immortal,
summoning the celestial heights.

This is the elixir path of *inverted refinement*,
by which immortality is achieved.
In essence, it is the return
from awareness to non-awareness—
another branch of cultivation.

This is the refinement of external elixirs
to cultivate internal elixirs,
returning from *post-heaven* to *pre-heaven*.

Let me speak plainly:
The Dao of birth follows the natural order,
the Dao of immortality inverts and overcomes—
for if it does not overcome, it does not give life,
nor can it achieve completion.
Thus, the *River Diagram* and *Luo Book* employ both generation and overcoming.

Now, the cultivation of Confucian and Buddhist scholars
differs from my Dao—
they follow the natural order,
conforming to the measure of spontaneity.
My Dao alone inverts and refines,
requiring strenuous effort and deliberate action.
If one fails to overcome,
there can be no birth or completion.

Yet cultivation in accordance with nature is easy,
while inverted cultivation is difficult.
Without a true master,
without the correct method,
reckless gathering and reckless refinement
rarely fail to bring harm.
Once a true master is obtained,
once the correct method is known—
if one does not seize the immortal opportunity,
if one does not perform virtuous deeds,
then the spirits of heaven will not aid,
demons will entangle,
and one will surely fail at the brink of success—
elixir overturned, cauldron shattered,
life and body both lost.
This is truly something to be cautious of!

How does one invert and overcome?
At first, one follows the natural order,
imitating the method of husband and wife,
with fire entering the water’s domain—
this is the spirit entering the *qi*—
this is the common father and mother producing the elixir.

When fire steams and water boils,
gold is born from the water’s depths.
At this time, the mystic orifice opens,
true faith arrives—
true yang is born, and the child elixir is produced—
this is the external elixir.

Once the gold *qi* is born,
true lead is sufficient.
With fire hastening and water surging,
wood bearing gold upward,
urging it step by step,
gently guiding it,
ascending to the *Kan* cauldron,
pairing true lead with true mercury,
using true fire and true intent to draw it down
into the elixir field,
entering the *Kun* womb—
with furnace and cauldron harmonizing the elixir substances,
this is the reversal of *Kan* as male,
the restoration of *Li* as female.

Reversing male and female,
selecting host and guest,
returning them to the furnace,
boiling and refining for a time,
then awaiting the movement of true yang fire,
to make the great elixir of gold and fire.

This is the birth of the internal elixir,
also called the birth of the great elixir.
This is the sacred father and holy mother
conjoining to bear it.

As for the earlier minor elixir’s birth,
its movement lies outside the kidney passage,
its *qi* is small—
thus it is called the *minor elixir*, the *external elixir*.
This, however, moves within the *qi* roots—
when born, there are celestial omens of stars,
earthly signs of tides,
and tremors in the six senses—
thus it is called the *internal elixir*, the *great elixir*,
also called *golden elixir*.

Again, with this golden elixir,
one stirs the *River Vehicle*,
agitates the *Xun* wind,
applies the *Kun* fire,
and refines the true essence of the *Li* palace.
True *qi* merges with true essence,
using *pre-heaven* yang *qi*
to subdue *post-heaven* yin essence—
the yin essence also merges with true *qi*
and transforms into the sacred embryo.

True *qi* is born from true essence—
this is the child *qi*—
*qi* returns to essence,
thus likened to the child entering the mother’s womb.
The child clings to the mother and comes,
the mother clings to the child and remains.
Child and mother embrace,
spirit and *qi* depend on each other.

Within, the true fire burns;
without, the *yin* and *yang* fires are applied—
internal and external refinement together
form the sacred embryo.
As it is said:
*"When lead is nearly spent and mercury dries,
it transforms into a single mass of purple gold."*

The great elixir path differs from the path of birth
only in its inversion of creation,
its reversal of heaven and earth.

All those with virtue, with fate, with the Dao,
who encounter this exposition,
may apply themselves without fear of heterodox calamity.

Yet the celestial secrets are fully revealed here.
If there are those who aid in virtue,
who receive celestial inspiration,
who understand this meaning—
they must not lightly divulge it,
lest they incur guilt.

「As for the scripture’s mention of *"the sovereign of ten thousand chariots"* (萬乘之主), it refers to the **original spirit** (元神) within the human body.

Indeed, no one’s heart does not wish for their own body to be at peace and their hundred years of life to be strong and unbroken. Yet how can one know the **Dao’s enticement** (誘物化) and the rise of emotions, while still recklessly expending their body for the sake of the world? This is **qi** (氣) that is hollow and dissipated, losing its essence; this is the **spirit** (神) that is restless and ungrounded, losing its clarity. Even if the body remains, its vitality is scarce indeed—how much more so for the **great elixir Dao** (金丹大道)?

This exposition has now meticulously clarified the principles of **foundation-building** (築基), **self-refinement** (煉己), **forming the elixir** (結丹), **returning the elixir** (還丹), **jade nectar** (玉液), and the **small and great circulation** (小大周天). Those of noble birth and scholarly standing should cherish and never forget it, lest they fail to grasp its truth and practice it to its fullest.

Thus, upon attaining completion and realizing the Dao, one becomes a **celestial immortal** (神仙) forever, free from the sufferings of the mortal world. Is this not most fortunate? Each should strive accordingly!

**Chapter Twenty-Seventh: Always Doing Good to Save Others**
To act in goodness without leaving a trace,
to speak in goodness without flaw,
to advise without need of calculation,
to close without latch or key yet unopenable,
to bind without cords yet unbreakable—
this is why the **Sage** (聖人) always does good to save others,
and thus never abandons anyone;
always does good to transform things,
and thus nothing is cast aside.

This is called **inheriting clarity** (袭明).
Thus, the good person becomes the teacher of the ungood,
and the ungood person becomes the **resource** (資) of the good.
If one does not honor their teacher,
nor cherish their resource,
though wise, they remain in great confusion.
This is called **the essence of subtlety** (要妙).

The **Sage’s** heart seeks only within themselves,
not from others.
In their application to affairs and things,
**non-action** (無為) yet nothing is unaccomplished,
and wherever they act, it is fitting—
within, they lack no self-fulfillment,
without, they cause no harm to others.

As the *I Ching* says:
*"When the time is to stop, they stop;
when the time is to act, they act—
neither movement nor stillness loses its proper moment,
their Dao is radiant and clear."*
Could this not be the **Sage**?

When it comes to action,
they act when the time is right—
that is all.
They see neither the source of their coming,
nor the destination of their going—
how could there be any trace?

Their goodness in action is such.

When it comes to speech,
they speak when the time is right—
that is all.
Within, they suffer no humiliation,
without, they bring no shame to others—
how could there be any flaw to be criticized?

Their goodness in speech is such.

As for matters requiring calculation,
or affairs needing deliberation,
they measure by **reason** (理),
and weigh by **humanity** (情).
They act in accordance with reason,
and cease when fitting with humanity—
when more is needed, they give more;
when less is needed, they give less.
Why bother with the labor of calculation?
This is **spontaneous response without contrivance** (因應無心),
where both self and others transform naturally—
what else could be called **good judgment** (善計)?

There are also matters that should be closed or bound.
For others, failure to close leads to chaos,
failure to bind leads to dispersal—
yet the **Sage** cuts off all external ties,
and no internal thought arises.
Complete and whole,
is this not what is meant by **good closure** (善閉)?

Though there are no cords to bind,
no keys to secure,
there is no gap to exploit—
it is as if sealed tightly,
and thus cannot be opened or undone.
Is this not **the natural perfection of the Dao** (天理浑全),
unassailable?

As for these principles,
they follow **the natural order of Heaven** (自然之天),
untainted by human contrivance.
Thus their effects are such.

In essence, they **cultivate inwardly** (內修) **while emulating outwardly** (外慕),
**self-correcting** (自正) **without seeking anything else**.
This is how they **establish themselves and others** (立己立人),
leaving no one abandoned;
**perfect themselves and transform things** (成己成物),
discarding no talent.

How great is their virtue in saving and benefiting others!
This is **not merely inheriting clarity** (重袭其明),
but also **extending it to govern and transform** (理民及物).

Yet the good person does not know themselves as good at first—
they forget the distinction between self and others,
so the ungood revere them as teachers.
The good person is also not self-satisfied—
when they see the ungood,
the good person takes them as **resources** (資).
They follow what is good,
and correct what is ungood—
thus, through this, the good person advances further in goodness,
until they reach the realm of **great transformation and divine perfection** (美大化神).

If common people rely on their own talents,
boast of their own abilities,
and ignore the good as if it were nonexistent—
not learning from them as models,
nor abandoning the ungood as worthless—
instead, they despise them and deem them unworthy,
not understanding that *"seeing the worthy, one should emulate them;
seeing the unworthy, one should reflect inwardly"* (見賢思齊，不賢內省).
Though good and evil differ,
they are both **teachers and resources for self-improvement** (師資).
Such people, who do not honor their teachers
nor cherish their resources,
are truly the **foolish and self-deluded** (愚而好自用，賤而好自專),
not the **enlightened** (昏昧人).

Goodness is what one learns from,
evil is what one takes warning from.
Wherever one encounters it,
it benefits themselves—
no one is without benefit to their body.
This is truly the **essential method for self-cultivation** (修己之要術),
the **wondrous Dao for governing the body** (治身之妙道).
Let all strive accordingly!

This exposition reveals the **Sage’s** words,
which encompass all things.

The principles of affairs and things
are none other than the **Dao of life and essence** (性命之道).
**Substance and function** (體用) are inherently unified,
**root and branch** (本末) never separate.

For instance, *"good action leaves no trace"* (善行無辙迹),
extended to the **flow of qi** (氣機流行),
the **self-moving celestial chariot** (河車自運),
is also such.

*"Good speech leaves no flaw"* (善言無瑕摘),
meaning there is no **method to be spoken of** (法可說),
this is called **spontaneous expression** (說法).
It is also said to be the **intention of the ancestors** (祖師西來意).

Confucius said:
*"Heaven speaks not, yet the four seasons move in their course,
and all things are brought to birth."*
If there are flaws to be criticized,
then there must be speech to be seen—
this is not the **Sage’s** true understanding of **heart and spirit** (心領神會).

The **Buddhist school** (釋氏) says:
*"The Dao is originally without words,
yet people have spoiled it by speaking of it."*
This is their meaning.

*"Good judgment requires no calculation"* (善計無筹策),
for the **circulation’s** (周天) numbers
are merely a metaphor for the three hundred transformations—
in truth, there are no **divination lines** (爻策) to calculate.
If there were, it would not be the **natural fire at its proper stage** (火候).

*"Good closure has no latch or key"* (善閉無關鍵),
meaning it is the **primordial chaos unbroken** (鸿蒙未破),
the **original spirit** (元神) silent and still,
the **original qi** (元氣) in profound obscurity,
returning to the **beginning of the Primordial** (元始之初),
to form the embryo and become the **Sage** (聖).」

If there is closure, there must be opening—
this is not the Dao of inner cultivation.

*"Good binding has no cords or ties,"*
for the spirit clings to qi and congeals,
life depends on nature and abides.
When spirit and qi harmonize,
they return to the **Primordial Polarity (Taiji)**,
forming the **millet-grain pearl**—
the body of the **Yang Spirit**.

If forced together, it is not natural congealing,
and one cannot thereby restore life to its true essence.
Yet such is its effect.

The essence of cultivation lies only in
turning toward the good when seeing it,
correcting faults when they arise,
learning from the categories of good and evil,
and reflecting inwardly to make it one’s practice.

If one boasts of talent, relies on intelligence,
despises the Dao and scorns others,
does not honor one’s teacher,
does not cherish one’s resources—
even with talent and wisdom,
one remains a foolish man,
unworthy of entering the Way.

Here lies the subtle key to cultivation:
the Sage and the common man share the same path.

---
**Chapter Twenty-Eighth: Constant Virtue Does Not Depart**

Know the **masculine** and hold to the **feminine**,
to become the **valley of the world**;
To be the **valley of the world**,
constant virtue does not depart,
returning to the **infant**.

Know the **white** and hold to the **black**,
to become the **model of the world**;
To be the **model of the world**,
constant virtue does not err,
returning to the **Ultimate**.

Know the **honor** and hold to the **humiliation**,
to become the **valley of the world**;
To be the **valley of the world**,
constant virtue is then complete,
returning to the **Uncarved Block (Pu)**.

The **Uncarved Block** scatters to become vessels;
the Sage uses them as **officials and leaders**.
Thus, the great **measure** is not cut.

The Dao of cultivation:
**qi** is born from the **Yang**.
Operate the **River Chariot (Hecarot)**, moving by **Child-Midday**.
When the **lead’s qi** is fully extracted
and the **mercury’s essence** is sufficient,
then lead and mercury merge into one **qi**—
this is when the **masculine** is united to forge the **elixir**,
but one must still **nurture the feminine** to nourish the **elixir**.

Thus it is said:
*"Know the masculine, hold to the feminine."*

The **masculine** is **Yang**; the **feminine** is **Yin**.
When **Yin** and **Yang** harmonize,
**masculine** and **feminine** interact,
and **gold is hidden in water**;
**water** again generates **gold**,
and when the **golden qi** is full,
the **tidal signs** arrive.
Its momentum is like a **valley stream**,
flowing downward from above,
like the **accumulation and exhaustion** of a ravine.

The cultivator knows that **Yang** does not arise from **Yang** but from **Yin**,
so one does not cling to the **masculine** but to the **feminine**.
Over time, subtle **Yang** gradually emerges,
**Yin dross** is fully transformed,
and the **constant virtue** of returning to the **Root** and restoring **Command** must never be separated for an instant.

From this, **Yin** and **Yang** copulate,
forming the **immortal embryo**,
and day by day, it is nurtured into the **infant**—
this is inevitable.
As the *Awakening to Reality* says:
*"Within the masculine, the feminine is embraced to form the sacred embryo."*

Once lead and mercury merge,
fusing into one,
take this copulating essence
and refine it in the **Kun Palace (Earth)**—
**true lead** is born.

This is called *"knowing the white and holding to the black."*
The **white** is **essence**; the **black** is **water**.
Before the **essence** is produced,
the **Kun body** is originally empty,
yet through union with **Qian (Heaven)**,
**Kun** becomes **Kan (Water)**.
Thus, **gold is born from water**,
nourished by the **Mother Qi**.
Hence it is called **Mother Qi**.
As the *Awakening to Reality* says:
*"From the black, take the white as the elixir’s mother."*

When **true lead** is obtained,
use a drop of one’s own **mercury** to welcome it.
Lifting left and right,
quietly await the **White Tiger’s** head passing through.
If one hears the **thunder beneath the earth**,
there is indeed the **elixir-heart piercing the sun**,
**overwhelming qi reaching the heavens**—
I remain steadfast in my **void-cave**,
not the least perturbed.
This is the time of **refining essence into qi**.

Afterward, operate the **wheelbarrow (lunlu)**,
ascend the **three vehicles (sanjia)**,
from the **double spine-gate** up to the **cinnabar field (daniwan)**,
following the **four cardinal directions (zi-wu-mao-you)**,
and aligning with the **four seasons**.
This is to be the **model of the world**.

All things—growth, contraction, storage, and return—
do not differ in the slightest from the **Heaven’s transformations**.

Thus, ascending and descending,
returning to the **earthly furnace**,
transforming the **manifest** back to the **unmanifest**,
returning to the **Ultimate Void**.
This is the **Great Circulation’s** moment—
the **jade liquid elixir** is here.

At this time, the **golden elixir** returns to the **mysterious orifice**,
merging with the **true unity of the Azure Dragon’s qi**,
refining into the **non-dual Primordial Spirit**—
this is the time of **refining qi into spirit**.

To cultivate further, the Dao of **refining spirit back to the void**—
only **mixed and indistinct**,
nurturing the **void**;
**blended and submerged**,
perfecting **principle and qi**;
transforming **discrimination into wisdom**,
becoming **holy yet appearing foolish**.

「Each day and night,
speak not lightly,
mind free of other thoughts—
like a simpleton,
utterly without knowledge or perception.

Though insults come in abundance,
stand as though unaware,
just as **Shun** dwelled in the deep mountains,
no different from a mountain recluse.

This is the **honor of the sage**,
the **humiliation of the immortal**.

Unless thus, one cannot **nurture the void** and **harmonize with the Dao**.

Hence it is said:
*"Open the mouth, the spirit-qi scatters,
disturbed thoughts chill the fire’s alchemy.
He who knows to return and restore—
his golden treasure weighs like mountains."*

If one rashly speaks a word,
or recklessly harbors a thought,
then one is like a thief of the elixir.

The Dao grows higher,
the path grows riskier.
At this stage of elixir refinement,
it is the most perilous terrain—
thus ancient masters,
after attaining **fruit of the Dao**,
feigned deafness and dumbness,
acted mad and deranged—
all for the sake of **nurturing the void** and **harmonizing with the Dao**.

Why else would they endure such suffering?

For the mind holds nothing,
this is the **ultimate valley** of the world.

As the **ultimate valley**,
one must further **cool the intent like ice**,
**clarify the heart as water**,
and only then can the **constant’s** mysterious **virtue/power** be fully realized.

Yet **true emptiness is not emptiness**,
**wondrous existence is not existence**.
At first, from **void** to **manifest**,
then from **manifest** to **void**,
until **void** and **manifest** stand not.

This is the **returning to the origin**,
**restoring to the Primordial Simplicity**—
the Dao of **Great Circulation** achieved.

Though, when gathered, it is one,
when dispersed, it is myriad.
In eternal generation,
in endless transformation—
where is not the **vessel’s** dwelling?
Where is not the **Primordial Simplicity’s** scattering?

This is the saying of **Primordial Simplicity scattering as vessels**.

The **sage** applies it:
not clinging to **vessels** yet scattering **Primordial Simplicity**,
meaning **void** and **stillness** rule as the **master of the body**,
the **total support of all transformations**—
like the world’s officials, none second.

And what is meant by *"the Great Measure does not cut"*?
It is the **Dao’s** all-encompassing embrace,
no excess in its bounds,
no distortion in its fulfillment—
sufficient for governance.
If it cuts, then it is artificial,
not the **original nature** of **Heaven**.

The **sage** does not cut,
merely returning to the **mixed and indistinct** **Heaven**.

Do scholars understand this?

If one examines **Confucius’** chapter on *"The Container of Virtue"* alongside,
then the essence of **refining essence**,
**refining qi**,
**refining spirit** is fully grasped.

Yet, its subtleties I dare speak of again:
*"Formerly, when I met my teacher,
he gave the oral precept:
‘Only concentrate spirit into the qi orifice.’"*

Unless one **returns the light** and **reflects the brilliance** to the elixir field,
then **golden water** will remain turbid.

Once knowing to **concentrate spirit in the Kundalini Palace**,
if one ceases the **constant practice**,
then **water and fire** will scatter,
and from where will the **Primordial Unity’s** **pre-heaven qi** arise?

Though **concentrating spirit** is essential,
**regulating breath** is no less so.

If one knows to **concentrate spirit in the qi orifice**,
yet fails to **regulate inhalation and exhalation**,
sending breath downward into the **yin cave**,
then though spirit may dwell,
breath will not flow freely—
no means to **fan the wind** and **stir the fire**,
to **still ordinary breath** and **reveal true breath**,
to **quell ordinary mind** and **awaken true mind**.

And since **spirit-fire** entirely depends on **spirit-breath**,
if **spirit-breath** does not blow,
not only will **water and fire** remain unclean,
but the **golden embryo** will fail to refine.

Once **spirit is concentrated** and **breath is regulated**,
one knows where to **return and restore**—
at the moment when **spirit merges** and **qi flows freely**,
like **Heaven** before its opening,
dark and indistinct,
then all wandering thoughts and turbid qi
can be gathered and purified,
just as the **sun and moon** undergo a cycle of eclipse,
revealing a new brilliance.
Thus, **silent and still**,
at the time of **no knowledge, no awareness**,
suddenly **knowledge and awareness** arise—
this is the **Great Circulation’s** foundation,
the **mysterious pass’s** manifestation,
the **first stir of yang**,
the **beginning of all things**.

If one can **seize this moment**,
**grasp it firmly**,
then it is truly the **handling of mist and clouds**.

The **elixir canon** says *"When the time comes, the spirit knows"*,
and *"The true child is active at the moment"*—
this is what is meant.

At this moment, one must **harvest it immediately**;
if delayed even slightly,
then **post-heaven knowledge and awareness** will intrude,
unfit for the **golden elixir’s** medicine.

This **critical juncture**,
one must **lay down all entanglements**,
**raise no thought**,
and swiftly seek with **true intent**—
only then does one obtain the **true pure medicine**.

One must **be still again and again**,
**sink deeper and deeper**,
and in the time of **no knowledge, no awareness**,
seek the place of **knowledge and awareness**—
then perhaps it will be found.

If one says *"no thought arises"*,
why then does one **seek with intent**?
Is it not that **seeking with intent** itself
falls into **post-heaven knowledge and awareness**?

Yet one does not know—
this **true intent**,
like a **hidden flame**,
not seen yet always present—
merely **moved by the mechanism**, the **spirit follows naturally**,
such is the **spontaneous response**.

If one says **true intent** is truly **intent**,
then it falls into **rigidity**.
If one says **true intent** is truly **no intent**,
then it drifts into **stubborn emptiness**.

Between **intent** and **no intent**,
the student must **awaken to this**.

The *I Ching* says:
*"Quietly still, yet unmoved,
it responds and thus communicates"*—
this is it.

Only then is **true knowing, true awareness**,
all driven by **true intent**.

Though, **true intent** arises from **true heart**,
one must have a **heart emptied and pure**,
its brilliance unincreased by **having**,
unlessened by **lacking**.
With this **true heart**,
only then is **true intent**.
With this **true intent**,
only then is **true breath**.

One must **possess insight**,
**never miss the opportunity**,
then each refinement yields its own **growth and benefit**.

At this stage,
if one **constantly harvests**,
then **true yang** will naturally emerge.
One must further **refine oneself** and **await the moment**,
never harboring even a hint of **forcing movement**,
then **post-heaven knowledge and awareness** will not intrude,
and the **pre-heaven’s** **ultimate yang essence**,
the **Primordial Unity’s qi**,
will through **long cultivation** accumulate—
then the **great medicine** will arise,
capable of **returning youth** and **reversing aging.**»

Only fear is the unwillingness to accumulate merit and practice to establish **external cultivation**.
Uphold propriety in conduct and refine the moral order to cultivate **inner virtue**—
this alone serves as the foundation for reception.

The common saying goes:
*"Not fearing one instance,
only fearing accumulation.
Not fearing suddenness,
only fearing contrivance."*
Truly, these words are wise.

The student who seeks to know the **Dao of intent** must not merely rely on spontaneity.

---
**Chapter Twenty-Nine: Eliminate Excess and Extremity**

*"If one seeks to take the world by force,
I see it as inevitable failure.
The world is a divine instrument—
it cannot be seized, cannot be grasped.
To act upon it brings ruin;
to cling to it brings loss."*

Thus, things either move or follow,
are drawn in or exhaled,
are strong or weak.
Therefore, the Sage eliminates excess,
eliminates extravagance,
eliminates excessiveness.

The **Dao** is originally without sound or scent,
pure and natural in its clarity.
The practitioner must also remain unknowing and unrecognizing,
purely yielding to nature—
this is the heart-seal of ancestors from antiquity to the present,
unalterable and beyond deviation.

Yet, the world’s heterodox sects mock our **Way** as solitary cultivation and silent refinement,
ultimately calling it stubborn emptiness and uselessness.
How could I not reflect upon this?

*"If one seeks to govern the world with active measures,
I see that the more one acts, the more inevitable failure becomes.
The world, though vast, is originally governed by the divine instrument.
What is called the **Primordial Dao** is the silent, natural one.
The world is the framework of the divine instrument;
the divine instrument is the sovereign of the world.
The world may be acted upon, but the divine instrument cannot be seized.
If one acts upon it, at first there is confusion and excess,
until restraints are abandoned and boundaries transgressed,
and **Heaven’s virtue** is utterly exhausted—
this is precisely why action leads to ruin.
How much better to succeed through **non-action** than to fail through action!
How much better to attain the **Dao** through non-attachment than to lose through attachment!"*

Since the **Dao** originates from **Heaven**,
and **Heaven’s Way** is **non-action**,
yet spontaneous transformation arises within it—
how could it be otherwise?

Observe the moment of birth:
The **Primordial Yang** initiates with **Heaven’s Element**—
sometimes **yang** moves forward first;
**Earth’s Element** sustains life—
sometimes **yin** follows afterward.
Motion and stillness interdependently root each other,
each with its necessity.

As for **qi**—
when extended, it bends inward, and inhalation arises naturally;
when contracted, it expands, and exhalation flows effortlessly.
Thus, **vital breath** flourishes,
and **generative vitality** endures forever.

Yet, due to differing endowments,
some are strong with abundant **qi** and robust **essence**,
others weak with scarce **qi** and feeble **essence**—
all these are disparities of **post-heaven** cultivation.
Since things are inherently distinct,
sometimes **qi** ascends vigorously,
sometimes it descends gently—
all these are the natural operations of **Heaven’s Way**,
beyond human contrivance.

Even at the outset, there may be traces of effort,
yet one must follow the momentum and align with the moment—
acting when appropriate, resting when due,
blending effort with spontaneity,
so that over time it remains unspent.

This is why the Sage, when gathering medicinal herbs or refining elixirs,
must eliminate what is already excessive,
eliminate what is overly extravagant,
eliminate what is overly extreme—
always returning to moderation,
constantly embodying harmony.
Though it may seem like **action**,
it is equal to **non-action**;
though it may seem like **doing**,
it is the same as **non-doing**.

Thus, **being** and **non-being** generate each other—
only then can one speak of the **Great Dao**.
This is the saying: *"The **Great Dao** is **non-action**"*—
**non-action** being the study of **nurturing innate nature**;
yet it also involves **action**—
**action** being the craft of **cultivating post-heaven life**.
One must know that **action** and **non-action**,
though differing in their names for cultivating **nature and life**,
share the same sovereign principle—
never to be moved arbitrarily,
for movement is deviation from the **Middle**.

Whether **action** or **non-action** is improper,
the key is to maintain the **Middle** without confusion,
to know the times and circumstances,
to advance when opportunity arises,
to retreat when difficulty comes—
then **non-action** is achieved,
and **action** is also attained.

What is this **sovereign principle**?
It is the **divine instrument of the world**.
If one knows the original source,
returning to **undifferentiated unity**,
**void yet luminous, unobscured**—
initially, **action** is necessary;
ultimately, **non-action** is necessary.
Otherwise, if one insists on **non-action** and spontaneity alone,
why did Confucius speak of the **Dao**,
why did he speak of **striving to practice**,
why did he speak of **choosing the good and holding fast**?

Know that the **Way of self-cultivation** lies in **nature and life**;
the **work of nature and life** requires balancing ease and effort,
not rigidly distinguishing them—
all depends on the **divine clarity of virtue**.

As in governing a state:
order is maintained through culture,
chaos through force—
responding to the times, acting in accordance with **Heaven**,
thus harmonizing left and right,
never failing to meet the occasion.

This is the **Dao** for the enlightened—
difficult to convey to the rigid and dull.

---
**Chapter Thirty: The Virtuous Achieve Fruit**

*"Those who assist the sovereign with the **Dao**
do not use force to dominate the world—
their affairs return favorably:
where the army encamps, brambles grow;
after great battles, there are years of famine.
Thus, the virtuous achieve **fruit** alone,
daring not to seek strength through it.
Achieve **fruit** without arrogance,
achieve **fruit** without boasting,
achieve **fruit** only when unavoidable,
achieve **fruit** without coercion.
When things reach their peak, they grow old—
this is called **not the Way**,
and **not the Way** perishes early."*

In the ancient world,
each ruler governed their own realm,
each remembered their people—
harmonious and bright,
sharing a peaceful **Heaven** without strife;
self and others forgotten,
boundaries dissolved in transformation—
how could there be warfare?

When shared labor led to chaos and warfare arose,
**Chiyou** rebelled against **Heaven**, and arms were raised.
Thus, culture had **jade and silk**,
martial arts had **weapons and armor**;
governance relied on **ritual and music**,
chaos on **spears and shields**—
hence, courts valued both **culture and martial virtue** equally.

Yet the **Dao**-aligned sage-ruler, enlightened and in high station,
assists the flourishing court,
