the *阳气* (*yángqì*, "yang-qi"—vital, ascending energy) sinks to the depths like the sea,
as if winter lingered into its final days—
all around, a profound stillness.

When the divine light descends to illuminate,
it is like the *阳* (*yáng*, "yang"—life-giving principle) emerging at the winter solstice,
yet the silence remains unbroken,
the walls stark and empty—
still, as before.

From this point, the breath of *气机* (*qìjī*, "qi-movement") gradually revolves,
and soon, the three yangs (*三阳*, *sānyáng*) flourish in harmony,
while all things return to the vitality of spring—
flowers crimson, leaves verdant,
water clear and mountains bright—
the peak of yang’s vigor is already evident.

The Dao of Heaven is thus.
What is the human body compared to it?

Only when one tilts the head slightly downward,
and gazes gently below,
does the *阴极阳生* (*yīnjí yángshēng*, "yin at its peak gives rise to yang") manifest.

At this precise moment,
it is not like the earlier effort—
grasping a single intent
and counting breaths.

One must now abandon the *外火* (*wàihuǒ*, "external fire"—artificial, forced energy),
halt the *内火* (*nèihuǒ*, "internal fire"—self-driven effort),
and let nature take its course without restraint—
yet not fall into old habits unknowingly.

This is the cultivation of the *存有觉之心* (*cún yǒu jué zhī xīn*, "mind aware of inherent existence")
to nourish the *无为之性* (*wúwéi zhī xìng*, "nature of Non-Action").

When awareness and illumination endure long,
and righteousness and benevolence mature,
what need remains for cultivation or restraint?
One need only abide in the natural order.

Otherwise, if at the outset one does not exert effort,
the wild monkey and untamed horse
may prove difficult to subdue in time.

Even when they come to submit,
one must not, as Mencius warned,
*"tie the pig after it has entered the pen"* (*放豚入苙*, *fàng tún rù yǒu*—i.e., impose rigid control once harmony is achieved).
To do so would only make them restless and uneasy,
forcing them back into resistance.

What then is the proper method?
The *I Ching* (*易*, *Yì*) says:
*"Heaven and Earth in their natural state,
and all things transform into purity."* (*天地絪缊，万物化醇* *Tiāndì gǒu yún, wànwù huà chún*)

「If this *gǒu yún* [絪缊] qi is cultivated within the body,
it is like stilling the inner fire and outer form,
remaining motionless and undivided,
allowing the breath to flow naturally.

For those whose practice is pure and refined,
one need not consciously hold onto it—
but if this stage has not yet been reached,
the mind of awareness must never be forgotten.

If forgotten, one risks drifting into habitual tendencies,
unaware of the ceaseless arising and passing of thoughts—
endless cycles of birth and death—
until the original, untainted essence
is swallowed by the very mind of generation and annihilation.

The ancient Buddhas taught:
*"Know the source of arising,
and you know the source of ceasing."*

Thus, one must nurture this awareness,
until over time the origins of arising and ceasing are seen,
and then, over time again, the state before any thought arises is glimpsed—
only then is it attained.

As for the teachings of the Yellow Court [黃庭],
they speak of neither presence nor absence,
neither inner nor outer;
yet they are also within the body of form,
yet not entirely within it.

Where lies this subtle secret?
The ancients said:
*"Concentrate the mind in emptiness,
and merge the qi in the boundless."*

To concentrate the mind in emptiness,
and merge the qi in the boundless,
is like dwelling in the elixir field [丹田],
yet not fixating the gaze inward to observe,
nor forcing the mind and qi to cling within.

Only by focusing the mind at the navel’s lower region,
not far from the flesh and skin,
does one achieve the "neither inner nor outer" state.

Directing intention there,
one feels the breath at mouth and nostrils cease,
while the elixir field’s qi
rolls and swells in the space where inner and outer meet,
knotted into a singular whole—
truly *gǒu yún* [絪絪缊缊],
undifferentiated and pure,
effortlessly rising and falling,
in perfect accord with Heaven’s primordial qi,
uninterrupted and seamless.

Here, essence, qi, and spirit are born,
close to the divine—
this is the "merging qi in the boundless" teaching.

The ancients called it *"primal qi"* [元气],
*"embryonic breath"* [胎息],
or *"the True Person’s breath reaching the heels"* [真人之息以踵].
What else could it be?

The *"primal qi"* is that undefiled breath
within the boundless, formless void—
a single, pure exhalation, clear and empty.

The *"embryonic breath"* is this:
when one first receives qi in the womb,
the body is nourished there,
mouth and nostrils yet unopened—
how then does it take in breath to live?

Only this navel-field qi,
communing with the mother’s navel-wheel [脐轮],
is why the child grows daily.

When the cry of birth pierces the earth,
and life begins outside the womb,
this qi flows in and out through the mouth and nostrils—
this is the *"each establishes their own heaven and earth"* [各立乾坤] principle.

I show that the navel-wheel’s qi
meets the external Heavenly breath,
neither fully inner nor outer,
*gǒu yún* [絪缊] and mingled—
a seamless fusion—
which is to return to the moment of first receiving qi,
and reconnect with the mother’s breath—
this is the embryonic breath.

The *"True Person’s breath reaching the heels"* means:
the True Person’s breath is stored deeply,
spreads subtly,
invisible, inaudible, untouchable—
deep and profound,
like qi extending to the soles of the feet.

The breath of mouth and nostrils is not useless,
but it must be allowed to act naturally;
one cannot rely solely on it for inhalation and exhalation.
If one uses only this breath
without first focusing the mind
at the navel’s lower region—
one inch and three *fēn* [分] below the flesh—
and seeking this void within the void,
to draw Heavenly qi into the infinite,
the result will be a mingling of purity and turbidity,
making alchemical refinement impossible.

The ancients said:
*"Heaven generates people with the One Primal Qi [一元真气],
which is neither mouth nor nostrils,
nor the subtle, sentient soul [灵] of knowing and moving."*

They also said:
*"The Mysterious Feminine Gate [玄牝之门] few know,
Do not waste breath through mouth and nostrils.
Though you practice inhalation and exhalation for a thousand ages,
How could you ever grasp the Golden Rooster seizing the Rabbit?"*
[金乌搦兔儿]

From these few lines alone,
it is clear that *"emerging from the Mysterious,
entering the Feminine"* [出玄入牝]
refers to the space
one inch and three *fēn* [分] below the navel,
where the qi *yīn yīn yūn yūn* [氤氤氲氲],
condenses into a single mass.

Those who study the Dao,
whether at meal times or in idle conversation,
must subtly direct a little intention,
focusing the mind in the void’s single orifice—
naturally merging qi in the boundless,
and seeing the True Qi move,
in ineffable wonder.

Yet in this breath regulation,
one knows the mind does not enter within,
and the Water of the Abyss [坎水] naturally clarifies.

This is the unspoken secret of generations of immortals and sages.
I now reveal it plainly—
later scholars must not dismiss it as empty words.

**Chapter 58: Calamity, Fortune’s Shadow**
Its governance is muted and unassuming,
its people pure and refined.

Its governance is sharp and scrutinizing,
its people restless and deficient.

Calamity, fortune’s leaning post;
Fortune, calamity’s hidden root.
Who knows their ultimate measure?
When the upright becomes the strange,
when the good becomes the demonic.

The people’s delusion has endured long.

Thus, the sage
is square without cutting,
honest without rigidity,
straight without excess,
bright without blinding.

Heaven and Earth transform without intent,
the sovereign rules without action.
This Way of Non-Action
is the great principle and law
by which the sage opened Heaven and Earth,
unified the world and ordered all things.

The ruler governs all people,
regulates all affairs—
nothing surpasses this.

If one indulges in action,
governance is not true governance,
rule is not true rule.
Though their writings gleam and their deeds shine,
they cannot achieve the harmonious, luminous state
where all rejoice in the flourishing and abundant transformation.

Thus, the *Tàishàng* [太上] says:
*"Governance is the rectification of the self"* [政者正也],
to correct others’ deviations with one’s own rectitude.

Since ancient times,
those who govern the people
have established human norms,
regulated Heaven’s order—
whether knowing or seeming ignorant,
whether acting or seeming inaction,
all let Heaven’s spontaneity move freely.

At first, there is no arbitrary cleverness,
no inventing of measures or rigid rules,
no hanging of laws or reading of edicts—
yet through the power of virtue,
a silent resonance arises beyond words.

---

Thus, their governance is **mùn-mùn** [闷闷], as if a simpleton without knowledge.
Yet the people’s trust and faith [感孚] are also **chún-chún** [淳淳], bearing the pristine winds of antiquity, unchanged in the slightest.

The ruler governs through **wúwéi** [无为], the people transform through **wúwéi** [无为].
Above and below share in the tranquil **Tian** [天] of no affairs,
resting in grandeur—how magnificent!

If the ruler strives with diligence [励精图治], exhausts his strength in governance [竭力谋为],
removes the wicked and evil [拔去凶邪], elevates the virtuous and talented [登崇俊杰],
records even minor kindnesses [小善必录], punishes great offenses [大过必惩],
and dispenses rewards and penalties without distinction—clear as ice and sharp as a mirror [赏罚无殊冰镜],
his oversight stern as divine judgment [监观俨若神明],
then his governance is **chá-chá** [察察], none escaping his discerning gaze [藻鉴].
Is this not weighty indeed?

Yet when the ruler demands excessive scrutiny [好苛求],
the people respond with cunning artifice [化为机巧],
fragile and hollow, each boasting their petty wisdom [缺缺然无不以小智自矜].
The ruler acts through **yǒuwéi** [有为], the people conform through **yǒuwéi** [有为],
and woeful is the difficulty of governing the people’s hearts!

For if the ruler does not purify the source [清其源],
then the people cannot rectify their roots [正其本].

Indeed, **wúwéi** [无为] is the **Tàishàng** [太上]’s original, undivided **zhēn** [真].
**Yǒuwéi** [有为] is the later, contrived **wéi** [伪].
The effects of **mùn-mùn** [闷闷] and **chá-chá** [察察] are thus utterly contrasting.

This is the **Dao** [道]—one alone, two is not.
Yet when the **Tàiji** [太极] of **xiāntiān** [先天] remains undifferentiated,
pure and undivided, there is no **yīnyáng** [阴阳] to name,
no **shàn’è** [善恶] to perceive.
The *Yìjīng* [《易》] says:
*"The simple is easily known, the unadorned is easily followed"* [易则易知，简则易从],
thus making governance vast and enduring.

If the **Tàipú** [太朴] of **hòutiān** [后天] is incomplete,
**yīnyáng** [阴阳] permeates its beginning and end,
and misfortune and fortune alternate as hidden dependencies [互祸福为倚伏],
with fortune within misfortune and misfortune within fortune,
then the cycle of **huòfú** [祸福] turns endlessly.

Thus, **yǒuwéi** [有为] is not necessarily unvirtuous,
but when things reach their limit, they transform;
when time reaches its extreme, it reverses.
The mechanism of **yīnyáng** [阴阳]’s interplay is inherently such.
Who knows the **dǐjí** [底级] and can steadfastly maintain the **zhèng** [正]?

Moreover, the **zhèng** [正] inverted becomes the **qí** [奇],
the **shàn** [善] repeated becomes the **yāo** [妖].
Governance through **wúwéi** [无为] is pure **Tian** [天].
Governance through **yǒuwéi** [有为] is mixed with **rén** [人].
Mixed with **rén** [人], the **zhèng** [正] contains the **qí** [奇],
the **shàn** [善] harbors the **yāo** [妖].
Its origins lie in subtle shifts [隐微],
its responses arise swiftly from echoes [影响],
and its momentum is indeed relentless [不容稍闲].
No wonder deceit and guile [尔虞我诈] become habitual,
a nature so ingrained that none awaken to it.
The days of this state have long passed.

Thus, the **Sage** [圣人] rules the **empire** [宇],
rooted in the **Dao** [道] of **wúwéi** [无为],
ordering his own conduct while guiding the people,
rectifying himself to transform others.
His **fāng** [方] is so natural that it seems no **fāng** [方] at all—
perhaps he attains **biàn** [变] and **tōng** [通] without recourse to artificial measures [裁截]?
His **lián** [廉] is so thorough that he forgets its existence—
perhaps he merges with the **sú** [俗] while remaining luminous and unblemished [和光不伤]?
His **zhí** [直] is upright, yet he neither blindly acquiesces [唯诺] nor recklessly follows his own desires [径情].
He adheres to principle and practice [认理行持], never daring to indulge himself.
His **gěnggài** [梗概] and **fēngguī** [风规] are truly worthy of reverence and awe.

As for his **transformation** [化] of all living beings,
his **en** [恩] extends to the four quarters—
nearly rivaling the radiance of stars and clouds,
vying with the heavens for brilliance—
yet he alone conceals his traces, never flaunting them.
How does he vanish his presence and extinguish his voice?

This is **wúwéi** [无为] as essence, **zìrán** [自然] as function.
To govern by aligning with desires [从欲以治],
to act by applying principle [须理以施],
so that the winds of the four directions move,
and none fail to flourish in the **yōng** [雍] of transformation,
all partaking in the **Tàigǔ** [太古]’s **Tian** [天].
Is this not the case?

The **Dao** [道] is called the **Dàdào** [大道],
**elixir** [丹] is called the **Jīndān** [金丹],
yet both are beyond **name** [名] and **xiàng** [象].
In **Tian** [天], it is the **qīngkōng** [清空] of **yīqì** [一气].
In **rén** [人], it is the **xūwú** [虚无] of **zìrán** [自然].
From **xiūliàn** [修炼]’s beginning to end,
its core remains no other than this.

If a person knows the **chōngmò** [冲漠] without traces is the **root of the Dao** [大道根源],
the **origin of the elixir** [金丹本始],
and from the **extreme of emptiness and profound stillness** [虚极静笃]
nurtures a **hún-hún** [浑浑] **lún-lún** [沦沦] state,
free from **knowledge** [知识] and **pènglǜ** [念虑],
then my **xìngqíng** [性情], **jīngqì** [精气], and **shén** [神]
are all matters of **xiāntiān** [先天]’s **Tàihé** [太和] **yīqì** [一气].
To **xiūdào** [修道] is to achieve **Dào** [道],
to **liàndān** [炼丹] is to perfect the **elixir** [丹],
and what is strange or perilous to fear?

But if one does not know **wúwéi** [无为] as the **foundation** [本],
and merely takes **yǒuwéi** [有为] as merit [功],
then **knowledge** [知识] never ceases,
and **fēnráo** [纷扰] grows ever more.
How could one not fall into the **hòutiān** [后天]’s **yǒuxíng** [有形] **yǒusè** [有色] **záwàng** [杂妄]?

The **Tàishàng** [太上] likens governance to the **Dao** [道],
and the people to the **body** [身].
When the **Dao** [道] refines **xiāntiān** [先天]’s **wúwéi** [无为],
it achieves the **unspoiled golden body** [不坏金身].
When the **Dao** [道] refines **hòutiān** [后天]’s **yǒushí** [有识],
how could it not result in the **duōyuán** [二元] **shén** [神]?

Even if refined well,
it is but the **shǒushíguǐ** [守尸鬼]—
how could it transcend **yīnyáng** [阴阳],
escape **shēngsǐ** [生死],
and eternally become the **immortal** [神仙] of all ages?

And yet, once one falls into **yǒuwéi** [有为],
the **Tàiji** [太极] is divided, and **yīnyáng** [阴阳] arises.
**Yīnyáng** [阴阳] separates, and **shàn’è** [善恶] emerges,
with **huòfú** [祸福] then interchanging.
Who knows that the **extreme refinement** [极功] of **Dao** cultivation,
though it may involve a **step of life-preservation** [炼命],
is not without the **use of yǒuwéi** [有为]?
Yet it must be through **yǒuyòng** [有用] to reach **wúyòng** [无用],
and through **yǒugōng** [有功] to attain **wúgōng** [无功],
only then does one avoid the **biānjì** [边际].

Mencius says: *"There must be affairs to attend to, but do not cling to them"* [必有事焉而勿正].
The **key to cultivation** [修道之要] lies precisely here.

Discussing the **human heart** [人心], one motion brings one stillness,
one **yīn** [阴] brings one **yáng** [阳].
**Yé** [邪] and **zhèng** [正], **shàn** [善] and **è** [恶]
are inherently cyclical, interdependent,
and ceaseless in their coming and going.
Thus, where there is **zhèng** [正], there is **yé** [邪],
and where there is **shàn** [善], there is **è** [恶].
Only when one returns to **húnwàng** [浑忘],
undivided and unseparated,
is there no **shàn’è** [善恶].

Otherwise, **zhèng** [正] inverted becomes **qí** [奇],
**shàn** [善] repeated becomes **yāo** [妖].
Zhuangzi says:
*"Heaven honors **wúwéi** [无为] as supreme,
while mortals burden themselves with **yǒuwéi** [有为]."*

Thus, even in the **time of yǒuwéi** [有为],
one must ultimately return to **wúwéi** [无为]
to avoid the **peril of tilting the cauldron** [倾丹倒鼎].

Alas, the common folk and vulgar scholars of this world
speak of **elixir** [丹] yet cling to the **dāntián** [丹田];
obstinately fixate on the **Héchē** [河车]’s path,
restricting themselves to the **body** [身]’s form—
their **understanding of wúwéi** [无为]’s essence has long been lost.

「Only the sage understands the Dao/Way of cultivation and refinement.
Though there are fire and stages, medicines and substances,
Dragon and Tiger, male and female,
cauldrons and furnaces, zithers and swords—
all manner of names and forms—
they are like the nets and snares used for catching fish and rabbits:
*When fish and rabbits are not yet obtained,*
*one must employ the nets and snares;*
*When fish and rabbits are secured,*
*the nets and snares are forgotten.*

If one clings to names and forms,
all are not the Dao/Way.

Thus, *when square, be square,*
*when chaste, be chaste,*
*when upright, be upright,*
*when bright, be bright—*
yet all must be wúwéi [无为],
shìwúshì [事无事],
returning to the undivided **húnwàng** [浑忘] of Heaven.

Let the scholar take the Dao/Way of wúwéi [无为] as natural essence,
establishing essence first before applying it in practice.
Even with **yǒuwéi** [有为],
it remains wúwéi [无为].

Do you know this?
Do you believe this?

**Chapter 59: Long-Life and Everlasting Vision**
To govern humanity and serve Heaven,
nothing surpasses **sè** [啬].
For **sè** [啬] is the early **fú** [服].
Early **fú** [服] is called **chóngjī dé** [重积德].
**Chóngjī dé** [重积德] conquers all.
To conquer all is to know no limits;
to know no limits is to have a realm.
A realm that endures is long-lasting.
This is called the Dao/Way of **shēngén jiǔshì** [长生久视],
deep-rooted and firmly established.

The Dao/Way of governing humanity is the same as serving Heaven—
for humanity and Heaven are fundamentally one **qi** [气].
Thus, serving Heaven does not go beyond governing humanity.
Do not say Heaven’s Dao/Way is distant—
it resides within humanity’s Dao/Way, so near.

If one does not know Heaven’s Dao/Way,
first observe the human heart.
To exhaust all human affairs is to align with Heaven’s Dao/Way.
Though high and low differ greatly,
as long as one prioritizes **ānmín** [安民],
Heaven’s heart unifies when the people are settled.

Its essence lies in valuing agriculture and the roots—
teaching the people to till and reap first.
For the people are the foundation of the state,
and food is their Heaven.
Once **sè** [啬] is practiced,
clothing and food will be abundant,
and the body and family will be secure.

As Mencius said:
*"Plant the five grains, and when the five grains are ripe, the people will flourish."*
And again:
*"The sage governs the world,
making grain and rice as plentiful as water and fire—
how could the people fail to be kind?"*

Thus, those who lead must urgently embrace **sè** [啬],
so the people may engage in joyful labor and dwell in peace,
nurturing life and honoring death.

There are those who, unseen and unheard,
early cultivate the hearts of the people,
who delight in their devotion as if feasting on the finest sacrificial meats.
This is **not speaking of virtue/power** [修德] yet virtue/power is cultivated,
**not speaking of upholding virtue/power** [尚德] yet virtue/power is upheld.

Even when plowing one-third of the land yields one harvest,
and plowing nine-tenths yields three harvests—
when grain and millet abound,
to make wine and sacrificial drinks,
to offer to ancestors and kin,
to perform all rites—
the virtue/power [德] thus accumulated is profound and weighty.
Who else but this can claim such virtue/power?

So, opening the Dao/Way of Heaven with great benevolence,
bestowing boundless blessings,
naturally aids the weak and attacks the benighted,
overthrows chaos and rescues the lost—
and conquers all it encounters.

Thus, all it faces are swept aside,
no one dares to meet in battle.
Not only does it pacify neighboring states,
but even distant lands and strange realms
are blessed with timely rains and harmonious relations.

Eastward it spreads, westward it advances,
northward it reaches, southward it connects—
its teachings extend to all four directions,
and who can know its limits?

Since it knows no limits,
the **imperial Dao/Way** [帝道] flourishes far and wide,
the **imperial vision** [皇图] is firmly established,
and the realm is secured.

The *Book of Han* states:
*"The Yellow River flows like a belt,
and Mount Tai gleams like a whetstone.
The realm endures in lasting peace,
and love extends to all descendants."*

Indeed, there is no deviation here.

When humanity governs a realm,
it has the means to obtain one—
and what is that means?
It is the **mother-qi** [母气] of the realm.
If there is no mother-qi,
how could one obtain a realm?

This is the fundamental ground—
what humanity should urgently study.

Before obtaining a realm,
one must seek the mother;
once a realm is obtained,
one must cherish the mother.
A realm’s mother is like a tree’s root,
or water’s source—
it endures long and never ceases.
This Dao/Way of governing the world
also applies to refining the body.

The scholar who practices the Dao/Way
can maintain **zhōngbǎo yī** [中抱一],
concentrate the breath, and regulate the spirit—
first seeking **yǒngzǐ** [汞子] to find **qiānmǔ** [铅母],
then nurturing **qiānmǔ** [铅母] with **yǒngzǐ** [汞子],
until **qiān** [铅] and **yǒng** [汞] unite,
child and mother merge,
returning to the original,
reverting to **tàipǔ** [太朴].
This is called the Dao/Way of **shēngén jiǔshì** [长生久视],
deep-rooted and firmly established.

Thus, one becomes **saintly** [圣] though ordinary,
**Heavenly** [天] though human.

The Dao/Way of refining the body
is not different from governing the world.
This is to govern humanity and serve Heaven,
to exhaust all human affairs and align with Heaven’s Dao/Way.
As it is said:
*"Humanity and Heaven are fundamentally one qi,
mutually responsive and harmonious.
The yang comes from the void above,
embracing me as master and sovereign."*

This is not an easy matter.

Its Dao/Way lies in **xūwú** [虚无],
its practice akin to tilling and reaping.
First, one **stores and nurtures**, **reflects and examines** [存养省察],
then **guides the nature to encompass emotions** [以性摄情].
When **water and fire merge** [水火混融],
and **kan and li harmonize** [坎离和合],
the **preheaven qi** [先天气] moves,
circulating through the **zhou tiān** [周天].
As it is said:
*"When the union of Heaven and Earth ceases,
a single point descends into the Yellow Court."*

This is to draw **kanzhōng zhī huáng** [坎中之潢],
filling the **void within li** [离中之虚].
Thus, the foundation of life is fortified,
and the **virtue/power of immortality** [人仙之功] is achieved.

This is like the practitioner of **sè** [啬]
who opens fields and clears land,
plows and harvests—
only then can one sow and cultivate the five grains.

From this, one further takes the **yin essence from li** [离中阴精],
sending it down into the **kan palace** [坎户].
Then, one merges the **yang qi from kan** [坎中阳气]
with the **yin essence from li** [离中阴精],
forming a single family,
seeding it in the **dāntián** [丹田] as medicine.
*"When others have none, I possess it;
when others are empty, I am full."*

Wait until true **qiānmǔ** [铅母] arises here—
then, with **yang qiān** [阳铅], one restrains **yin yǒng** [阴汞],
so its **flying nature** [好飞者] does not scatter;
and with **yin qiān** [阴铅], one nurtures **yang qiān** [阳铅],
so its **sinking disposition** [好沉者] does not descend.

The *Awakening to Reality* [《悟真》] says:
*"In the golden cauldron, retain the scarlet mercury,
In the jade pool, first descend the silver from the water."*

When the **qiān** [铅] and **yǒng** [汞] fly and float,
like dust particles in sunlight streaming through a clear window,
each drifting away—
until the **residual yang from kan** [坎府外之余阳] is fully absorbed,
returning to the **li palace** [离宫],
and the **private yǒng** [阴汞] and **personal recognition** [私识] are completely digested,
restoring the **pure yang treasure** [纯阳至宝] of the elixir.
This can ascend to the **Hàn** [汉] and pierce the heavens,
fly with the spirits and walk among the saints—
when the **shén tāi** [神胎] is formed,
and the **xiān yīng** [仙婴] is complete.

「Though the practice is not easily attained! One must first **cultivate resolve and nourish qi** [持志养气], like a farmer plowing and weeding—
not without toil and hardship.
Yet in the end, the **spirit is tranquil, the qi settled** [神闲气定].

Within, the **single principle** [一理] is complete and undivided;
without, one adapts to circumstances, ever balanced.
This is not a fleeting act—
it aligns with the **Dao/Way** [大道] when truly undertaken.

Through refining **nature** [修性] and tempering **life-force** [炼命],
one has already prepared the **submissive guest** [以宾服后起] to meet future causes,
and all burdens vanish, leaving no trace behind.
One fulfills **human virtue** [人道] to merge with **heavenly power** [天德],
not something achieved in mere morning or evening.

Like a nation’s governance,
it rests on **sincere integrity** [赤诚求],
**deep compassion and abundant virtue** [深仁厚德],
rooted in the people’s hearts,
penetrating to the marrow—
its virtue accumulates without end,
its weight knows no limit.

Thus, what one seeks to **exclude** [无不除] is never left undone,
what one strives to **overcome** [克] is never left unattained.
With **heavenly embrace serene and settled** [天怀淡定],
one walks the **Five Phases** [五] in calm assurance.
Whether in **change** [处变] or **constancy** [处常],
one moves in **preordained station** [素位],
never without **finding ease in all things** [无入而不自得].

If one applies this to **refine nature** [炼性], **nature is perfected** [性尽];
if to **cultivate life-force** [修命], **life-force stands firm** [命立].

In the **void of boundless emptiness** [冲漠无朕],
all **phenomena** [万象] rise in full array—
truly, there is none who knows its ultimate depths.

The *Tàishàng* [太上] says:
*"Internally observe the heart, yet the heart has no heart.
Externally observe the body, yet the body has no body.
Distant observation of all things, yet things have no things.
Empty of all that is empty, void of all that is void—
there is no void, nor is there any that is not void."*

Those who can **awaken to this** [悟], may **transmit the sacred path** [传圣道].
This is the **"externalizing the body yet the body remains"** [外其身而身存]—
the **body as a nation** [身犹国也].

Just as a **sage-ruler governs without action** [王者无为而治],
yet stands upright at the **southern face** [正南面],
and holds **nation and world** [有国有天下].

Similarly, **yin essence** [阴精] resides within one,
long mingled with the **father’s essence** [父精] and **mother’s blood** [母血].
Without the **primordial yang qi** [先天阳气],
it cannot **self-generate and grow** [自生自长].

For **postnatal yin essence** [后天阴精],
its origin is from **primordial qi** [先天],
but **yin essence is hard to retain** [阴精难固],
and **emotions and desires are easily unsettled** [情欲易摇].
Without the **earthly-heavenly external yang qi** [天地外来灵阳之气],
one cannot **condense and form the elixir** [结而成丹],
nor achieve **immortality and non-death** [长生不死].

Thus it is said:
*"The mother of a lasting realm,
can endure forever."*

Only the **sage** [圣人] unites **true yin and true yang** [真阴真阳],
the two **qi** into **one** [一气],
and **refines** [煅] a **drop of millet** [黍米]—
this is called **golden elixir** [金丹],
**true qiān** [真铅],
and the **White Tiger’s First Scripture** [白虎首经].
Its essence is none other than **primordial qi** [先天一气].

From the **form-body** [色身], through **endless refining and washing** [千烧万炼，千磨万洗],
gradually **extracting and condensing** [渐采渐凝],
sometimes **simmering, sometimes refining** [时烹时炼],
the **golden elixir** [金丹] is formed—
**luminous and complete** [英英有象],
the **so-called "stealing the earthly-heavenly qi to use as elixir base"** [人盗天地之气以为丹母].

This is the **rooted and enduring path** [深根蒂固],
of **long life and lasting vision** [长生久视].

To **combine the earthly-heavenly luminous yang** [天地灵阳]
with **one’s own true qi** [一己真气],
and **form the sacred embryo** [结成圣胎],
the ancient **Daoist immortals** [仙] say:
*"When the **primordial yang first stirs** [先天一阳初动],
one **moves a drop of innate mercury** [运一点己汞] to greet it."*

Thus, **inner contact and outer stimulation** [内触外激] yield **form** [有象],
**outer contact and inner resonance** [外触内感] bring **spirit** [有灵].
Like **magnet attracting iron** [磁吸铁],
they **naturally align** [自然吻合].

The **mercury child** [汞子] **constructs the water palace** [造水府],
seeking the **qiān mother** [求铅母].
Once the **mother is obtained** [得其母],
it **relies on the child** [复依其子].

**Child and mother in harmony** [子母和谐],
**clustered in the central palace** [团结中宫],
the **great elixir is complete** [大丹成],
and the **path of immortality is realized** [神仙证].

The **beginning and end, root and branch** [本末] of elixir refinement,
the *Tàishàng* [太上] has already **exhaustively taught** [道尽].
Scholars must **attend closely and grasp its meaning** [细心体会].
Though **traces and symbols may seem similar** [迹象虽相似],
there are **great distinctions in essence and refinement** [精粗大有分别].

Yet until the **right moment** [其时] arrives,
one cannot **know** [知].
Without a **true teacher’s guidance** [真师指授],
there is no way to **illuminate** [明].

This requires **heavenly, earthly, and human connections** [天缘地缘人缘],
the **three causes converging** [三缘凑合],
before one may **enter the chamber and begin work** [入室行工].

Later scholars must first **accumulate sincerity and cultivate virtue** [积诚修德],
**empty oneself to seek a teacher** [虚己求师],
only then may the **three causes be united** [结三缘] and entry gained.
Do not **take joy in mere attainment** [一得自喜],
for then there will be **no aspiration to ascend** [无向上之志].

**Resolutely pledge and surrender** [矢志投诚],
**with all strength pressing forward** [一力前进],
**step by step, unceasingly** [迤逦做去]—
this is acceptable.

At the very outset of practice,
there is **no crack to enter, no gap to seize** [无缝可入，无隙可乘],
just as **chewing wax pills** [咀嚼蜡丸]—
**bland and tasteless** [淡泊无味].

Zhū Zǐ [朱子] says:
*"In learning, one must **strive with vigor** [猛奋],
**endure patience in self-realization** [体认耐烦辛].
Toil through the day,
and in time, **bitterness yields to sweetness** [苦尽甘来],
**suppression gives birth to joy** [闷极乐生]—
then **the Dao advances and the mind finds clarity** [道进而心有得].

At this juncture,
when **principle and desire ride together** [理欲杂乘],
and **heavenly and human forces clash** [天人交战],
it is most difficult to act.

Its **advance and retreat** [进退] hinge on this **passage** [关].
If this **passage is broken through** [关攻得破],
then **Confucius’ words hold true**:
*"The splendor of the ancestral temple,
the wealth of all officials,
the endless enjoyment of rewards"* [宗庙之美，百官之富，赏玩之不置].

Do not **wilt and falter** [萎靡不振],
nor **let one’s own spirit weaken** [自家精神放弱],
for then one will **never enter the gate** [终身不得其门而入] in this lifetime.

Most importantly,
**empty the mind** [虚其心],
**expand the resolve** [大其志],
**stir the spirit** [鼓其神],
and **establish virtue and function** [立德立功],
**refine nature and temper life-force** [修性修命].

Know that this is the **greatest matter between heaven and earth** [天地间第一大事],
and without **great strength** [大力量], it cannot be accomplished.

In days past, there was a couplet:
*"Brace iron shoulders to bear **Daoist rectitude** [道义],
Unfurl trembling hands to craft **sacred texts** [文章]."*

Ah!
Even in the world,
a **single talent or skill** [一材一艺],
or the **pursuit of minor scholarly fame** [小小科名],
requires **toil and endurance** [辛苦耐烦].
To **achieve great deeds and virtues** [大功德],
one must **employ a full measure of true spirit** [满腹真精神],
only then may **heaven and the divine favor** [神天默佑] be invoked,
and **its fruits observed** [观厥成].
How much more so for the **Dao** [道],
the **greatest matter of heaven** [天大一件事]!

Thus the **Buddha** [佛] says:
*"I descended into this realm for the **great cause and connection** [大事因缘].*
*So too do I."*

Scholars who have **met a true teacher** [遇真师],
must **grasp my words with sincere heart and true intent** [以真心诚意体认],
only then may they be counted as **great men of the world** [人间大大丈夫].

**Chapter Sixty: Two Do Not Harm Each Other**
To govern a **great realm** [大国] is like **cooking fresh delicacies** [烹小鲜].
To **apply the Dao to the world** [莅天下],
its **spirits are not uncanny** [其鬼不神].

It is not that its **spirits are not uncanny** [其鬼不神],
but that its **spirit does not harm** [其神不伤人].
It is not that its **spirit does not harm** [其神不伤人],
but that the **sage also does not harm** [圣人亦不伤人].

Because **two do not harm each other** [两不相伤],
**virtue returns in mutual accord** [故德交归焉].

The **Dao** [道] is the **shared principle** [共有之理]
of all **heaven and earth, beings and things** [天下人物].
To **refine oneself with this principle** [修身],
is to **govern the world with this principle** [治世].

To establish oneself is to establish others; to reach oneself is to reach others.
Without waiting for a change of thought, without needing to delay time—how easy and simple it is!

Thus, the **Supreme Sage** said: *"To govern a great realm is like cooking fresh delicacies."*

When a realm is great, its affairs must be numerous, its people many. If one does not grasp the **Dao**, then matters will inevitably become chaotic and convoluted—like trying to untangle disordered silk, the more one tries to govern, the more tangled it becomes.

Only by refining oneself with the **Dao** shared by all—governing the multitude with this same principle—do the **principles** align, the **qi** flow uninterrupted, and the governance become effortlessly effective.

Otherwise, relying solely on laws, decrees, stratagems, and technical measures to command the world—when openly enforced, it breeds resentment among the people, and their hearts grow deceitful and multifarious; when secretly imposed, it provokes the wrath of the **spirits**, and calamities and disasters multiply.

For humans are the sovereigns of **ghosts and spirits**. When rulers impose heavy taxes and cruel tyranny, leaving the people with no refuge, then **ghosts and spirits**, lacking any attachment, must stir up omens and portents—famine, pestilence, and misfortune follow inevitably.

Thus, the **stone spirit** appeared in **Jin**, the **comet** in **Qi**, the **serpents fought** in **Zheng**, **Bo You** became a vengeful ghost, **Shen Sheng** was haunted by spirits, the **Two Rascals** fell ill beyond cure, **Shen Xin** descended, and **Guo** was destroyed—though these were said to be the work of **ghosts and spirits**, they were truly the result of the ruler’s lack of the **Dao**.

If those who rule the people truly refine themselves with the **Dao** and transform the people with the **Dao**, then even the most **obscure and stubborn spirits** will naturally gravitate toward them—no grievances arise among the people, no disasters from the **ghosts**. Mountains and rivers remain unscathed, no strange phenomena appear, and all enjoy a flourishing peace.

The *Book of Documents* says:
*"Our ancient kings diligently cultivated their virtue.
There were no celestial calamities—mountains, rivers, ghosts, and spirits were all at peace."*

Is this not because the **spirits are not uncanny**?
For **demons and spirits**, mountain **precincts** and water **monsters**, all depend on some attachment, require their offerings, and follow their natural course without interference. Even if there are **spirits**, they have nothing to manifest; even if they manifest, how could they cause harm?

Thus, **yin** and **yang**, humans and **ghosts**, all play and frolic under the bright heavens—how could they harm anyone?

It is not that the **spirit does not harm**, but that the **Sage**, possessing the **Dao**, lacks the prying intelligence of the overly perceptive and the self-aggrandizing benevolence of the overly sentimental. They carefully refine themselves, uphold natural relationships, maintain reverence in action and simplicity in conduct, avoiding all unnecessary complexity—never causing the slightest harm to others.

When **yin** and **yang** are harmonized, the people and all things flourish; when rituals are honored, **ghosts and spirits** are at ease. In the unseen realm, there is no mutual intrusion. Thus, all under heaven willingly submit to the **Sage’s virtue** and return to its accord.

Ah! The governance of **non-action** is drawn near from the self and far from all things. The unknowing and unknowing—this is the **Way of the Emperor**. Compared to those who rely on strict decrees and harsh punishments, hoping for diligence through fear—who is more difficult, who is more burdensome? The difference is as vast as heaven and earth!

Why do people not seek the fundamental principle?

This is the **great realm** illustrating the **great Dao**, just as **cooking fresh delicacies** illustrates **alchemical refinement**. Fresh delicacies—such as lamb, fish, and meat—are cooked only with soy sauce, vinegar, salt, and plum sauce, balancing the five flavors. Supporting what is deficient, restraining what is excessive, and gently nurturing with warm fire, the flavors emerge naturally over time, pleasing both body and palate.

Refining the **Great Elixir** likewise requires harmonizing the four **symbols**, gathering the five **phases**, making the three **blossoms** converge in one **cauldron** and the five **qi** gather in the central **field**. Then, the natural divine fire slowly nurtures—no need for artificial adjustment, no forced manipulation. It proceeds naturally, and in seven returns and nine revolutions, it is as easy as turning one’s palm.

The ancients said:
*"Slowly tend the alchemical furnace, watching the fire’s nature,
Only rest the spirit and let heaven’s work unfold naturally."*

How effortless it is!

Thus, the **Dao of non-action** is the **Dao of ruling the world**, and it is also the **elixir of Great Return** for refining oneself.

In a **Great Peace**, governance reaches its highest principle—regulations are light, the people transform naturally. Above, there is **non-action**, yet all is governed; below, there is **non-action**, yet all is transformed. All **ghostly omens and malevolent spirits** vanish without a trace—not that they are annihilated, but that they naturally dissolve into the **Dao of non-action**, their deceits and transformations having no place to manifest. Droughts, floods, plagues, and epidemics cannot arise.

In the human body, **ghosts** are the **yin**, still and unaware; **spirits** are the **yang**, dynamic and active. For those who cultivate greatly, the mind encompasses all things yet remains without mind, emotions respond to all things yet remain without emotion. **Yin** contains **yang**, **yang** contains **yin**—stillness without stillness, motion without motion. Motion and stillness interact; **yin** and **yang** mutually root each other.

It is not that there is no awareness in unawareness or action in non-action. Rather, within unawareness lies awareness; within non-action lies action.

When it is said, *"its spirits are not uncanny,"* it is not that they are dull and lifeless. For the awareness within unawareness is the **true and equal awakening**; non-action in action is the natural unfolding of heaven’s will. How could it compare to the deceptive awareness of the overly conscious or the rigid adherence of the overly active, which would harm the **original elixir**?

When it is said, *"its spirit does not harm,"* it is not that the **spirit does not harm**, but that the **Dao of non-action** preserves the innate **true nature** of life and the ceaseless **numinous qi** of existence—uninterrupted sincerity, encompassing all things without omission. Though there may be creation and destruction, there is no true loss or gain; though there may be fullness and emptiness, there is no true increase or decrease.

The so-called *"unperturbed and unalarmed,"* *"without worry or concern"*—this is it.

And how could it harm others? It is not that the sage does not harm others, but rather that with the **vital force** of spontaneous vitality, he preserves the **original true nature**; with the **harmonizing trance** of the Three Mysteries, he nurtures the **free-flowing elixir**. At once, the **divine fire** refines, and the ghosts wail while the spirits cry out, the malevolent retreat in submission—**the True Person** emerges.

This is called *"the two not harming each other,"* who could say otherwise? Both in heaven and among men, all praise its **virtue**.

Ah! The interplay of darkness and light—**not the virtue of the spirit**, how could it reach such heights?

**Chapter Sixty-One: The Great Must Descend**

The great state descends to flow beneath,
a gathering place for all under heaven,
the **receptive** of all under heaven.

The **receptive** always takes the **creative** through stillness,
stillness as the foundation of descent.
Thus, when the great state descends beneath the small state,
it takes the small state;
when the small state descends beneath the great state,
it takes the great state.
Hence, either it descends to take,
or it descends while taking.

The great state seeks only to **harbor** all people,
the small state seeks only to **submit** and serve others.
When both attain what they desire,
the great state is fitting to descend.

The **Supreme Sage** speaks of cultivating the Dao and refining the elixir—
all must take **gentleness** as the principle,
stillness as the essence.

Though it may be said that *"gentleness and passivity are useless,"*
and *"solitude and seclusion are hard to accomplish,"*
yet at the outset of seated meditation,
one must first arise from stillness,
rigidity from gentleness—
only then is the **true and equal Dao** revealed.

The analogy: *"The great state descends to flow beneath,"*
speaks of water having high and low—
the high water must flow downward before it ceases.

If the great state humbles itself and restrains its ambition,
with no thought of arrogance or deception,
it will be admired by all under heaven—
like the low-lying land where all streams converge,
its influence is inevitable.

Thus it is said: *"The gathering place of all under heaven."*

When all under heaven gather,
it is because they can descend themselves.
Descending, their **qi** is most **gentle**—
not the utmost **rigidity**.

Which among things is more **creative** than the **creative**?
Which is more **receptive** than the **receptive**?

The **creative** is yang, **rigidity**;
the **receptive** is yin, **gentleness**.
Thus, it is fitting that the **creative yang** should surpass the **receptive yin**—
yet why does the **receptive** always overcome the **creative**?

It is because the **receptive** can attain stillness.
The ancients said: *"Stillness governs movement,"*
their words are unerring—
just as the low supports the high,
its influence is inevitable.

How much more so for the great state,
which descends to **nurture** itself,
is **humble** to **protect** others,
and yet all states come to **revere** and **submit**?

Thus, descending is the basis of **high** virtue,
stillness the root of descent.

From ancient times to the present,
sometimes the great state descends beneath the small state—
like **Tang the Victorious** descending to **Bo Ge**,
ultimately taking **Bo Ge’s** lands,
**nurturing** and **possessing** them—
this is the case.

Or the small state descends beneath the great state—
like **Gou Jian** submitting to the **King of Wu**,
ultimately taking **Wu’s** legacy,
**harboring** and **possessing** it—
this is the case.

Or the great state does not act great but acts small—
thus it takes the small state as effortlessly as turning one’s palm.

Or the small state remains content in its smallness and serves the great—
thus it takes the great state as easily as picking up a blade of grass.

Discussing the **proud and mighty** great states,
they are truly the models for all states,
**nurturing** and **calming** with method,
**embracing** and **reconciling** with strategy—
not desiring to swallow all under heaven,
to unify the land by force,
but rather to **harbor** the small states,
to make all under heaven a single family—
only those with **great virtue** beyond others
can **rest** and **contain** with ease.

Thus, it is fitting that all under heaven should **return** to **Ren**,
all directions **submit** to the **Mandate**.

The **petty and insignificant**,
all equally part of the **feudal division**,
as vassals offering tribute in fear and trembling—
not desiring to **exalt** themselves to **humble** others,
nor to **preserve** their lineage by **prolonging** their rule,
but only to **submit** and **serve** to **fulfill** themselves,
to **extend** the **respite** of the common people—
only those with **great wisdom** beyond others
can **restrain** themselves and descend with ease.

Thus, it is fitting that the people’s hearts **love** and **revere**,
the **Mandate** comes to **return**.

Moreover, men must have **aspirations** and **desires**,
the great state desires to **harbor** all people,
the small state desires to **submit** and **serve**—
both desires, one of **Ren** and one of **wisdom**,
have already attained what they seek,
without straying into the **private desires** of men—
this shows that great and small states,
by **name**, follow their **principle**,
**settle** in their **allotted roles**,
and none dare **transgress** their duties.

Although the small state descends,
its principle is inevitable;
the great state, especially, must **dwell** in descent—
only then does the **True Person** begin to **stand erect**,
becoming the **reliance** for all under heaven.

Thus is the **Age of Peace**—
how different is the **cultivation** of the body?

*"The great state"* is an analogy for the **original spirit**,
*"descending flow"* for the **divine light** descending to illuminate the **elixir field**,
while the **yin essence** also descends into the **elixir field**,
the **divine fire** refines—
the essence transforms into **qi**, which then generates **spirit**.

This **elixir field** is the **original pass**.

The **elixir field** is the **total support** of the body,
the **convergence** of the five **qi**,
the **condensation** of the three **blossoms**—
where the elixir forms and the **spirit** gestates,
where the **spirit** emerges and the **sage** is born—
all refining occurs within this single **pass**.

Thus it is said: *"The gathering place of all under heaven,"*
like all rivers converging at the sea—
here is where the elixir is refined.

And the method of **combining medicines**,
again values **gentleness** and **flexibility** as the core—
thus it takes its symbol from the **receptive** of all under heaven.

The **receptive** is **gentleness**, **harmony**—
the **Supreme Sage’s** **Dao**, also called *"concentrating qi to achieve gentleness."*

In such **utter gentleness** and **harmony**,
the **original essence** flows freely,
transforming into **qi** to generate **spirit**.

Moreover, the **original essence** resides within—
stillness **cultivates** the **kidney qi**,
until the **divine fire** refines,
the essence transforms into **qi**,
and then the **reverse cultivation** technique is applied—
**ascending** and **swallowing** it,
returning it to the **earthly crucible** to **lead refine mercury**,
thus **using the creative to govern the receptive**—
this is the **River Vehicle** and beyond.

If at the **beginning of cultivation**,
the heart is **externally yang** and **internally yin**,
the **kidneys** are **externally yin** and **internally yang**.

「Speaking of the post-heavenly form,
the heart’s external yang is the *male* (社),
the kidneys’ external yin is the *female* (牝).

Now, when the *emptiness of the Receptive* (离中虚) becomes yin,
and the *fullness of the Abysmal* (坎中满) becomes yang,
it is as the *Awakening to Truth* says:
*“Though others may be the host, I am the guest”*;
and again:
*“Though yang is the male body of a woman,
yin, though the female body, is the male essence.”*
This is the inversion of Heaven and Earth—
the Receptive reversed becomes the *male*,
the Abysmal reversed becomes the *female*.

The method of cultivation seeks to
transform the heart’s rigidity into gentleness,
its agitation into stillness;
to transmute the kidneys’ softness into firmness,
its stillness into motion.

Thus, the Receptive’s gentle harmony
nourishes the Abysmal’s fierce yang—
this is *“fire within birthing wooden fluid,
water within forging adamantine steel.”*
By the heart directing the *qi*,
and by nature tempering the passions—
when emotions do not move recklessly,
it is only through silence and gentleness,
humility and yielding below.

This refines the heart’s nature.
Hence, the *upper field’s* sweet nectar
flows into the *primordial sea*;
the fluid then transforms into *qi* and enters the *elixir field*.

*“The great realm yields to the small realm”*
refers to the descent from the upper field to the lower.
*“Taking the small realm”* means extracting the *golden water qi* from the elixir field,
reversing it through the *River Vehicle*,
and ascending to the *celestial pass*—this is so.
*“The small realm yields to the great realm”*
is again descending from the lower field to *Kunlun*—this is so.

To take the *great realm* is to merge Kunlun’s golden fluid,
returning it to the *Yellow Court*.
I take the upper field’s sweet, pure nectar,
flowing it into the lower elixir field to generate *qi*—
then to extract the elixir field’s *qi* is to take from the great realm below.
Or, the elixir field’s *qi* ascends in reverse to the celestial pass to generate fluid—
swallowing the celestial pass’s *qi* is to take from the small realm below.

This is the golden water ascending,
the lead-qi merging with marrow,
the essence condensing, the *qi* harmonized—
in an instant, transforming into sweet dew, divine water,
flowing to the upper palate,
drop by drop returning to its source—
this is the moment when fluid transforms into *qi*.

When the *qi* mechanism is robust,
again operate the *River Vehicle*,
sending it upward to Kunlun,
swallowing the brain’s sea marrow and essence,
then descending back to the Yellow Court—
this is when *qi* transforms into fluid.

Yet, *“the great realm is the downward flow”*—
with gentleness and stillness,
resting with boundless capacity,
truly surpassing others in measure—
this is when spirit transforms *qi* and *qi* refines essence,
filling the elixir field.

Thus, the *desire to nurture others’ virtue*
possesses the small realm’s inner clarity,
knowing its strength cannot rival,
willingly submitting to serve—
truly surpassing others in magnanimity.
This is when essence generates *qi*, *qi* generates spirit,
also returning to depend on the Yellow Court.

Thus, the *way of serving others*.
Both desires are without external longing—
so the elixir completes its nine transformations,
the Dao ascends to the ninth heaven,
eternally enduring alongside Heaven and Earth.
What then is the exchange of its virtue?

The subtle key to cultivating the self
finds no equal to this.
Those who attain it treasure it—
do not lightly divulge it.

**Chapter Sixty-Two: The Dao is Most Precious to the World**

The Dao is the mystery of all things,
the treasure of the virtuous,
the safeguard of the unvirtuous.
Fine words can be traded,
noble conduct can be bestowed upon others.
What is there to discard in a person’s unvirtue?
Thus, though one may have a wall to block swift horses,
it is not as good as advancing this Dao.

Why was this Dao held most precious in antiquity?
Was it not to seek and obtain,
to avoid guilt and escape punishment?
Thus, it is most precious to the world.

The Great Dao arises before Heaven and Earth,
mingles within the void and formlessness,
dim and indistinct—
visible yet unseen, heard yet unheard, grasped yet untouched—
yet truly that upon which all things depend for life.

Zisi said:
*“The way of the noble is costly and hidden.”*
Without the Dao, there is no thing;
without things, there is no Dao.
The Great Cycle’s boundaries,
refined into the finest dust—
it cannot be sought through traces or symbols,
cannot be exhausted by speech.
Truly, it contains the utmost void yet embraces the utmost reality,
the utmost emptiness yet encompasses the utmost substance—
vast and boundless, profound and unfathomable.
No mystery surpasses this.

The virtuous know this Dao is the most vital to the human body,
so they cherish and conceal it,
cultivate and treasure it,
never willing to part from it even for a breath.
The unvirtuous also know that with the Dao,
life may be preserved and fortune attained,
but without it,
life is hard to prolong and calamity abounds.
No better strategy exists for preserving the body.

Moreover, if this Dao of *the Middle Way* is expressed in speech,
it becomes *fine words*—
like precious goods sold in the marketplace,
which all love and covet,
desiring to possess.
If this ordinary Dao is manifested in conduct,
it becomes *noble action*—
like the stature of a great lord,
which all respect and honor,
each elevating it above themselves.

If it cannot be spoken of,
its market reverses into disgrace;
if it cannot be practiced,
its bestowal invites slander.

The *Odes* say:
*“Heaven nurtures the people,
establishing things with their proper norms.
The people’s inherent nature
loves this virtuous power.”*
This shows that though good and evil differ,
their love of virtue is one.

Seeing the virtuous, I should revere them.
Even seeing the unvirtuous—
how can I hate them?
It is only that their *qi* and nature are occasionally skewed,
their desires not yet refined,
and thus they stray from the Dao.
Yet their source is ultimately unchanging.

If one can transform and guide them,
even the most wicked may turn toward goodness.
Great indeed is Heaven and Earth’s rejection of nothing,
the Sage’s rejection of no one.

If there are those rejected,
it is self-rejection—
how could the Daoist endure to cast them out?
Heaven creates the people and establishes rulers over them,
making them teachers,
so that they may govern the world and set the Three Ministers—
all to统驭 the common folk,
to transform and guide the masses.
Correcting oneself to correct the court,
correcting the court to correct the world.

「Let the myriad lands harmonize in unity,
and may the winds of the four quarters stir in accord,
so that the Son of Heaven may long preserve his august dignity,
and the Three Ministers may long enjoy their noble rank—
only then shall he rest.

If one cannot uphold the Dao as Heaven’s way,
to renew and sustain the people,
how could one ever permanently secure Heaven’s mandate,
and enjoy boundless blessings?

Even with the splendor of arched walls before him,
and fine carriages drawn by four steeds behind,
he cannot find a moment’s ease.

How much better to approach the Dao daily,
ever vigilant at dawn and diligent at dusk,
never forgetting, but sitting in its embrace!

The *Chu Book* says:
*"The treasure of Chu is none other than goodness—
goodness alone is the treasure."*

The *Shang Book* says:
*"Treasure only the virtuous,
and the common folk shall be at peace."*

This is the Dao—
the most prized by ancient emperors, kings, ministers, and officials alike.

Why did the ancients hold this Dao in such esteem?
Because the Dao is the inherent path of all people,
one who seeks it shall find it,
and its pursuit is swift and effortless.

If one upholds this Dao,
he becomes a true man of worth;
if one defies and betrays it,
he becomes a great offender against Heaven and Earth.

Is it merely that he has faults
and cannot avoid straying into error?
Zisi’s son said:
*"The Dao must never be abandoned for an instant."*

Let men strive earnestly!
For the Dao is a great matter in life—
whether Son of Heaven or Three Ministers,
all should cherish and hold it dear.

Even with arched walls and four-horse carriages,
they are not as beneficial as mastering the Dao.
Do not say, *"I am too aged,
my qi too diminished,"*
and thus excuse oneself—
this is not acceptable.

Though gold elixir and jade elixir
may require the refinement of post-heaven *qi*, essence, and spirit
to attain immortality and sainthood,
they are not the core of our teaching.

The ancients spoke of *"Great Harmony as the Dao,"*
and again of *"Emptiness-Nothingness as the Dao."*
Thus, if one does not grasp the principle of Emptiness-Nothingness,
or the Dao of Great Harmony,
even if he refines essence and subdues *qi*,
enters the realm of non-duality (*feifei*),
still he will differ not from the common man.

Therefore, in our Daoist practice of elixir cultivation,
one must take the Primordial Spirit (*yuánshén*) as the master,
and the Primordial *Qi* (*yuánqì*) as the assistant to the spirit,
using true breathing as the means to forge the elixir.

Without the Primordial Spirit,
there is no foundation for the elixir;
without the Primordial *Qi*,
there is no aid to refine it.

This is like a fetus having a child within it—
without the union of father’s essence and mother’s blood,
it remains empty and unformed.

Once the Primordial Spirit and *Qi* are obtained,
without true fetal breathing (*táixī*),
the spirit and *qi* cannot coalesce in one place,
merge as a single whole,
and return to the original state of Great Purity (*táisù*).

I impart this further truth:
When a person practices cultivation,
having obtained the Primordial Spirit and *Qi*,
and possessing true breath to regulate,
he must gather the five into four,
and merge the three into one.
Yet without true intention as the guiding commander,
the energies shall scatter and disperse,
never spontaneously uniting to form the elixir.

But whence does true intention arise?
It must come from the state of utmost Emptiness and profound stillness,
when there is no knowing and no awareness—
suddenly, the *qi*-mechanism is touched,
and awareness begins.
This is the true intention,
not the same as ordinary mind or ordinary intention.

Thus the ancients said,
*"Sainthood is not attained by others—
only by this one who cultivates without attachment."*

Yet without the gold within water,
and the *qi* within essence,
as aids to support it,
even the Primordial nature remains suspended and ungrounded,
and may fall into dull, inert voidness.

Once knowing the birth of the elixir,
without true breath to regulate and refine,
how could one gather and cook it into the elixir?

Thus, true breath is the essential tool for elixir cultivation,
and true intention is the sovereign ruler of true breath.

For those who have not yet attained unity of spirit and *qi*,
how can they achieve stillness and concentration?

Once spirit and *qi* are returned to their command,
they must be deeply fermented—
only then shall the elixir be fully realized.

Do not dare to arouse the bright, aware mind,
for this shall only cause separation between wood and metal,
and block the interaction of *kàn* and *lí* (water and fire).

I use this to illuminate the mysteries of the Dao—
later scholars who grasp its meaning,
let them cherish and guard it carefully!

**Chapter Sixty-Three: The Great as the Non-Great**
To act in greatness is to act in non-action (*wúwéi*),
to do in doing is to do in non-doing (*shìwúshì*),
to taste in tastelessness is to taste the Dao.

Great and small, much and little—
to repay resentment with virtue.

To attempt the difficult in its ease,
to achieve the great in its minute.

The most difficult things under Heaven
must be begun in simplicity;
the greatest affairs under Heaven
must be rooted in the smallest details.

Therefore, the Sage never acts in greatness,
and thus can accomplish the great.

He who makes light of his promises
shall be found lacking in trustworthiness;
he who seeks much shall encounter many difficulties.

Thus the Sage treats difficulty as difficulty,
and so shall he never face true difficulty.

The Dao is inherently the Middle Way (*zhōngyōng*),
one that all may learn,
and each may attain.

Yet because of the obstruction of things
and the constriction of *qi*,
if one does not forcefully cut away these hindrances,
how can he penetrate and see the original face of reality?

Like washing clothes—
long stained by dust and filth,
one cannot remove it in a single step.
It must be gradually scrubbed,
delicately plucked,
only then can the ragged cloth be made whole and new.

If one uses too much force,
not only shall the filth not be removed,
but the garment itself may be torn.

Thus the practitioner who seeks to penetrate the fundamental truth,
how can he fail to proceed step by step?

At first, he must strive and discipline himself,
without reckless haste;
with time, he grows natural in the Middle Way,
and sees the original nature of Heaven.

When his work reaches the stage of refining Emptiness and uniting with the Dao,
he acts in non-action;
when he responds to the Dao in its natural way,
he does without doing.

Plain and unremarkable,
what taste can there be?
Without taste,
what can there be to weary of?

As for the great going to the small,
the waning yielding to the waxing,
until the point of retribution—
this is not done with resentment,
but with virtue.
All these are the utmost transformations,
the complete fulfillment of cause and effect.

Yet in applying this,
he is even-handed without bias;
in repaying resentment with virtue,
there is no strange sentiment.

Moreover, virtue is the shared goodness of all people,
to repay with virtue is to act with the natural,
pure, and untainted spirit of man.»

Conforming to the Way of things, governing people with humanity,
even in matters of greatness and smallness, excess and deficiency,
all align with the movement of Heaven—
each moment is the Dao,
everywhere without deviation,
yet never conflicting with oneself,
nor offending others.

Alas, this Dao is both supremely difficult and supremely easy,
both supremely vast and supremely minute.

Yet worldly cultivators, seeking swift results and immediate effects,
often pursue what is difficult,
delight in what is grand,
unaware that difficulty lies in ease,
and that the foundation of the great lies in the small.
Thus, all great undertakings in the world must begin with the minute.

How much more so the Dao, the root of all things and affairs?
Can it not be approached by first mastering ease before difficulty,
and smallness before greatness?

Otherwise, those who advance too swiftly will retreat just as quickly—
how then could they hope to attain the realm of divine transformation?

Therefore, the sages of old knew that the Dao has stages to ascend,
that learning has a path to progress.
They did not contemplate distant grandeur,
but focused solely on the immediate essence,
refining dross, nurturing the source—
like water seeping into grass and wood,
naturally changing day by day, month by month,
growing without visible growth.

Thus, from the subtle beginnings,
from the crude to the refined,
from action and affairs to non-action and non-doing—
the more insipid, the richer;
the nearer, the farther—
until the attainment of sublime greatness.

The sage never seeks the great directly,
and thus achieves it.

Today’s scholars, at their very outset,
already aspire to become immortals.
The greater their ambition, the harder the task,
and most falter halfway through.

Only by persevering with steadfast endurance,
by maintaining an unyielding, ceaseless resolve,
can the difficult become easy,
and the great be grasped through the small.

I urge scholars to seek difficulty in ease,
to achieve greatness through the minute,
to proceed with measured patience and maturity,
lest they rush to recklessness and superficiality.

Otherwise, not only will they fail to grasp the Dao’s profundity
by cultivating a heart of sincerity and depth from the start,
but even in their most trivial promises,
those who act lightly will lack trustworthiness,
and their regrets will only deepen.
Those who seek ease will often encounter difficulty,
and retreat will follow swiftly—
this is inevitable.

Thus, the sage’s cultivation begins with ease and smallness as its foundation,
yet remains ever diligent and cautious—
this resolve never wanes.
By first addressing what is difficult,
later progress becomes as smooth as pushing a boat downstream,
acting without effort—
thus it is said, *"In the end, there is no difficulty."*

These three phrases—*"For non-action"*
—are the pure work of spontaneous alignment.

What follows—*"Seeking difficulty in ease"*
—expresses the intent that profound mastery must begin with the shallow and near.

As for the Alchemical Way,
speaking of lead and mercury—
what are these things?
Let it be clarified:
This matter concerns only the two poles of yin and yang.

When mercury is paired with lead,
it is as the female paired with the male.
After their union, primordial *qi* is generated,
then this *qi* is merged with yin *qi* in the central palace,
and thus the elixir is formed.

In the primordial state, *Li* (離) is the pure yang of *Qian* (乾),
and *Kan* (坎) is the pure yin of *Kun* (坤).
When the *qi* mechanism moves,
the central *yao* of *Qian* enters *Kun*,
and the central *yao* of *Kun* enters *Qian*’s cavity—
*Qian* thus becomes empty and turns into *Li*,
while *Kun* becomes solid and turns into *Kan*.
Hence, though *Qian* is yang, it contains yin,
and though *Kun* is yin, it contains yang—
yet it is not the original pure yin, pure yang, or the undifferentiated *Tai Ji*.

Still, it remains authentic.
With time, the spirit generates essence,
and *qi* transforms into blood,
giving rise to the nature of substance and *qi*,
and the fate of life’s measure.

Since there is a mind with thought and awareness,
and a body of *qi*, blood, and form,
it differs from the original *Qian* and *Kun*.

The adept, through methodical cultivation,
draws the single point of *yi* mercury from *Li*’s center—
(mercury is heart fluid;
though fluid belongs to yin,
it arises from *Li* fire and carries its nature)—
and descends it into *Kan*’s palace,
infusing *Kan*’s single point of yin blood—
(blood is *Kan* water;
though water belongs to yang,
it emerges from *Kan* water and is essentially cold)—
as the ancients said:
*"Fire enters the water domain,"*
*"Spirit enters the *qi* realm."*
Like ice encountering fire,
or charcoal heating a pot,
it naturally warms, generating a pulsating *qi* of yin vitality.

Though fire enters water,
it is like adding charcoal beneath a pot—
the rising heat steams upward in vigor,
and true lead is born.

Guided by the spirit, it ascends to the *niwan* (cinnabar field)—
just as alcohol vapors rise in a heated still,
condensing into dew that drips into the jar—
(which is what our teaching calls *"true mercury,"*
or *"Hurry, pour the North Sea’s first tidewater
to nourish the old tree’s roots"*).
In truth, *qi* has transformed into fluid.

Returning to the furnace for warmth and nourishment,
the fluid again becomes *qi*,
cycling endlessly in ascent and descent,
until the body of *qi* and blood is exhausted,
yin *qi* is stripped away,
and the mortal form is transmuted into a golden body,
the turbid transformed into the pure,
restoring the original *Tai Ji*—
the law-body of non-arising and non-perishing.

The late Zhu Yuan Yu once said:
*"When speaking of *Kan* and *Li*,
the essence of *Li* and the *qi* of *Kan* within the body
are both vulgar lead.
Only when *Kan* and *Li* unite,
and true yin and true yang converge,
does a single point of true yang emerge—
this is the seed of primordial true lead.
Yet without a master’s oral instructions,
even if one forcibly restrains it,
one can only preserve the color of the body.
When the lower *dan*tian is full and strong,
it will inevitably collapse over time.
The student who attains this yang birth
has only completed half the work—
how could they hope to gestate and become a sage?

Only by drawing this yang *qi* upward,
merging it with the body’s yin essence,
and further combining it with the spirit marrow and essence fluid of the *niwan* and *jiangong* (vermilion palace)—
this is truly *"The eastern household’s daughter (wood mercury),
the western neighbor’s son (gold lead),
uniting as husband and wife in the nuptial chamber."*

The Yellow Mother urges drinking *tíhú* wine,
each day perfuming and steeping in intoxication’s embrace.

This is the union of *Yīn* and *Yáng* to forge the *Dān*—
what came before was merely *Kǎn* and *Lí* merging to yield the medicine.

With this true *qián* (true lead) and true *gǒng* (true mercury) united,
only then can one refine the *huándān* (returned elixir).
For *qián* is the gold born from water,
and *gǒng* is the wood born from fire.
What came before was but common lead and common mercury—
now, this is the true *qián* and true *gǒng*.

If the student follows this path,
cultivating the *shén* (spirit) without agitating the *qì* (breath),
then perhaps they will not err in their endeavor.

**Chapter 64: Effortless and Non-grasping**
*Wúwéi wúzhí* (effortless and non-grasping) is fundamental and easy to uphold,
its unmanifested state easy to plan for,
its fragile nature easy to shatter,
its subtle essence easy to disperse.
Act before it arises,
rectify before it becomes disordered.

A tree of embrace—begins from a hair’s end;
a nine-tiered terrace—begins from piled earth;
a thousand-*lǐ* journey—begins beneath one’s feet.
Those who act bring ruin,
those who grasp lose hold.
Thus, the sage acts without effort,
and so knows no ruin;
grasps nothing,
and so loses nothing.
The people’s undertakings
often falter just as completion nears.
To be cautious at the end as at the beginning—
then there will be no ruinous affairs.

Thus, the sage desires without desiring,
does not prize hard-to-obtain treasures;
learns without learning,
reverses the errors of others.
To aid all things in their natural unfolding,
without daring to interfere.
The *Dao* of cultivating the self
begins with restraining desire.
The key to restraining desire:
to rectify it before it manifests is easy,
to rectify it as it begins to manifest is difficult;
to rectify it when it is manifesting is still more difficult,
to rectify it after it has manifested is hardest.

Hence, the *Tàishàng* (Supreme Sage) says:
*“Its settled state is easy to uphold,
its unmanifested state is easy to plan for.”*
When one resides in quiet solitude,
the mind not enslaved by affairs,
affairs not disturbing the mind,
still and unmoving,
settled in its place—
then upholding oneself and guarding the body
is most effortless.

Moreover, in silence and obscurity,
without knowing or awareness,
no trace or sign to seek—
here, to devise plans and ponder,
to banish idle thoughts and preserve sincerity,
its momentum is most natural,
its opportunity most ripe.
For common *qì* is soft and fragile,
common mind is subtle and fleeting—
not yet entangled without end,
not yet turning ceaselessly—
here, to break through perverse thoughts,
to scatter the seeds of desire,
and restore the natural *Dao* of Heaven,
the sincerity of the uncontrived—
how difficult could it be to sever the bonds of karma
and instantly reveal the original nature of the self?

This is not some separate act of effort—
it is merely *“acting before it arises.”*

「The ancient sage sought to prevent calamity before its sprouting,
to scrutinize the signs when movement was imminent—
thus sweeping away all smoke and clouds,
leaving no thorns or brambles to grow.

Again, when the world was at peace,
even if a tyrant or minor rogue
seized the moment to cause disorder,
it was no difficulty for a lone horseman to emerge,
see instant surrender,
and quell the disturbance before it took root—
its ease was indeed so great.

This discipline of self-refinement is still relatively attainable;
but if one seeks to perfect the **Nine Transformations**,
it cannot be measured by years and months.

How many are the ordinary, mundane folk
who do not know that the **Dao/Way** is the great path of Heaven and Earth,
and that humanity is the true person of the cosmos!
Some may chance upon a **dharma** assembly
and attain fulfillment in a single lifetime;
some may miss the right **karmic conditions**
and require several lifetimes before completion;
some may undergo repeated cultivation and many trials,
encountering fortunate circumstances,
yet fail to perfect their **virtue/power**—
their nature perverse, their disposition flawed—
they nearly succeed, then fail,
and in failing, never attain.

Truly profound are the mysteries of the **Great Dao/Way**,
not easily fathomed!

If one does not know the **Dao/Way** has its own means of realization,
let them observe how things come to fruition:
A tree with arms to embrace—
its origin was but a tiny sprout—
through the nurturing warmth of yin and yang,
changing daily and monthly,
grows into a great tree.

A nine-tiered tower—
its foundation was merely piled earth—
through human labor and diligent gathering,
ever renewing and flourishing day by day,
suddenly becomes a towering edifice.

Or, as with a unified realm of rivers and mountains,
a thousand *li* of territory to traverse—
could one expect to reach it with a single step,
or measure the journey by days?
Its beginning is but one step at a time,
from near to far,
until at last one arrives.

The **Dao/Way** is called great,
for it truly encompasses the vastness of Heaven and Earth,
the capacity to nurture all beings—
how could it not require layered effort to attain,
or winding progress to unfold?

Only those who deeply grasp the **Dao/Way**
do not seek swift results,
do not measure progress by near gains—
though gold and jade may be polished,
their resolve remains unpolished;
though seasons change,
their diligence does not wane—
thus, they grow from small to great,
from low to high,
from near to far,
just as the tree with arms to embrace,
the nine-tiered tower,
or the thousand-*li* journey—
and suddenly reveal wonders beyond compare.

Yet, the **Dao/Way** is the **natural Dao/Way**,
and its attainment requires **natural virtue/power**—
Mencius spoke of **"gathering and nurturing"** (*jìyì shēngqì*) **[1]**
to achieve effortless fulfillment, unceasing renewal.

At first, it aligns with the **Heaven-Earth transformations**,
yet its radiance remains ever the same as the sun and moon.
If one acts with contrivance,
the act will fail;
if one grasps with attachment,
the grasper will lose.

Heaven and Earth, the sun and moon—
eternally turning without cessation—
do they not achieve their transformations without effort?
If Heaven and Earth labored to cycle endlessly,
or the sun and moon clung to movement,
how could they endure for ten thousand ages?

The saying goes:
*"If Heaven had emotions, Heaven would grow old;
the sun moves without intent, yet its light remains constant."*
Is this not the truth?

Thus, the ancient sages
refined the **Dao/Way** with utmost precision,
harmonizing perfectly with nature’s flow.
They acted without contrivance—
their **virtue/power** never failed;
they grasped without attachment—
what loss of **virtue/power** could there be?

Yet today’s practitioners of the **Dao/Way**
mistake **non-action** (*wúwéi*) for mere inaction,
sometimes acting, sometimes abandoning—
they do not know when to move or when to rest,
when to align with the natural rhythms,
or when to stray far from them.
Some nearly perfect their attainment,
then suddenly falter,
and in faltering, never complete it at all.

The *Classic of Documents* says:
*"Be cautious of its end,
for it begins with the first steps."*
Thus, it endures through countless ages without decay.

As for rare treasures,
which people value highly—
the sage blends with the common, his light unassuming,
no different from others,
yet he seeks the **Dao/Way** and not wealth.
At first, he does not even know
that the world holds such treasures as precious,
so he does not prize them—
his detachment and clarity of purpose are thus.

Otherwise, in matters of sight, hearing, speech, and action,
in daily customs and conduct,
those who abandon moral restraint and indulge in licentiousness
need not be spoken of—
even among those who pursue the **Dao/Way**,
whether they cling to emptiness or solidity,
to attachment or non-attachment,
all are errors.

Now, I alone follow the methods of the ancients,
embrace the **Dao/Way** of old,
and express my own views—
not to claim they surpass all others,
but to weigh the **Great Dao/Way** as a standard.

The **Dao/Way** is my own **Dao/Way**,
learning is my own learning—
I find it through myself,
and it is self-attained—
what need is there for further study?

Moreover, people often err in their actions,
while I alone act without contrivance.
With my **Dao/Way** of non-action,
I correct the excesses of others—
this is to rectify myself in order to rectify others.
And with my **Dao/Way** of non-action,
I assist all things that fall short—
this is to regulate my own conduct
and lead all beings by example—
my reverence for such rectitude is thus.

The sage’s person is the **Dao/Way**’s dwelling,
the foundation on which all beings depend—
how could he pause even for a breath?

At the outset, when I spoke of
*"its ease in upholding and guarding"* and the following lines,
I referred to the **Mystic Pass** (*Xuānguān*) **[2]**
—a single aperture where,
in perfect stillness, one is moved by sensation alone.

Even in moments of **non-perception** (*bùdǔ*) and **non-hearing** (*bùwén*),
here lies the true essence of neither good nor evil.
The Buddha called it **"that"** (*nāgarā*),
the Confucian said **"gathering and nurturing"** (*jìxī*).
Both speak of this same reality.»

---
**[1]** *Jìyì shēngqì* (集義生氣): A phrase from Mencius, often translated as "gathering virtue to generate the vital force" or "accumulating righteousness to invigorate moral energy."
**[2]** *Xuānguān* (玄關): A term in Daoist and Buddhist meditation referring to the "mystic gate" or "gate of the profound," a metaphor for the gateway to enlightenment or spiritual realization.

「Like the morning sun upon lotus and willow,
the tender crimson and fresh green in dawn’s breeze—
so delicate and lovely in their bloom.

The *Yì* says:
*"Heaven and Earth in their primal union,
all things refined in their pure transformation.
Male and female in their union of essence,
all things born in their natural generation."*
**[3]**

This speaks only of the **initial qi** (*chūqì*) **[4]**
soft as dawn, still close to Heaven’s Way.
Zhūzǐ’s verse declares:
*"A half-acre pond opens like a mirror,
where Heaven’s light and clouds’ shadows drift and linger."*
**[5]**

Here, the **Dao-heart** (*dàoxīn*) **[6]**
and **human heart** (*rénxīn*) **[7]**
are clearly distinct at a glance.

To **hold fast to this resolve** (*chízhì*) **[8]**
and **nurture the qi** (*yǎngqì*), **[9]**
to **establish the teaching** (*lìjiào*) **[10]**
and **sever entanglements** (*gēduàn qiānhán*), **[11]**
to **ascend the other shore** (*dàn dēng bǐ’àn*) **[12]**
—all this is possible.

The *Lǐ* says:
*"Humans are born in stillness,
this is Heaven’s nature."*
**[13]**
Yet when stirred by things,
this is the nature of desire.

Like Heaven and Earth at the **primordial unity** (*yīyuán chūfù*), **[14]**
all phenomena returning to spring’s renewal.
Though things interact and desires stir,
they are still matters of Heaven’s nature,
rooted in **emptiness and stillness** (*xūjìng*), **[15]**
and aligned with the natural Way.

One need only **gently restrain** (*qiěqiě bǎchí*) **[16]**
without great effort of wisdom or strategy—
